Utah Code Annotated - Title 48 - Unincorporated Business Entity Act
===================================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 48 - Chapter 1c - General Provisions
****************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1c-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1c-101(1): This title is known as the "Unincorporated Business Entity Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1c-101(2): This chapter is known as "General Provisions."


Utah Code Annotated - Title 48 - Chapter 1d - Utah Uniform Partnership Act
**************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter may be cited as the "Utah Uniform Partnership Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(1): "Business" includes every trade, occupation, and profession.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(2): 48-1d-501 "Contribution," except in the phrase "right of contribution," means property or a benefit described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(3): "Debtor in bankruptcy" means a person that is the subject of:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(3)(a): an order for relief under Title 11 of the United States Code or a comparable order under a successor statute of general application; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(3)(b): a comparable order under federal, state, or foreign law governing insolvency.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(4): "Distribution" means a transfer of money or other property from a partnership to a person on account of a transferable interest or in a person's capacity as a partner.  The term:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(4)(a): includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(4)(a)(i): a redemption or other purchase by a partnership of a transferable interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(4)(a)(ii): a transfer to a partner in return for the partner's relinquishment of any right to participate as a partner in the management or conduct of the partnership's activities and affairs or have access to records or other information concerning the partnership's activities and affairs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(4)(b): does not include amounts constituting reasonable compensation for present or past service or payments made in the ordinary course of business under a bona fide retirement plan or other bona fide benefits program.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(5): "Division" means the Division of Corporations and Commercial Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(6): 48-1d-306(3) "Foreign limited liability partnership" means a foreign partnership whose partners have limited liability for the debts, obligations, or other liabilities of the foreign partnership under a provision similar to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(7): "Foreign partnership" means an unincorporated entity formed under the law of a jurisdiction other than this state which would be a partnership if formed under the law of this state.  The term includes a foreign limited liability partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(8): "Jurisdiction," used to refer to a political entity, means the United States, a state, a foreign country, or a political subdivision of a foreign country.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(9): "Jurisdiction of formation" means, with respect to an entity, the jurisdiction:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(9)(a): under whose law the entity is formed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(9)(b): in the case of a limited liability partnership or foreign limited liability partnership, in which the partnership's statement of qualification is filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(10): 48-1d-1101 "Limited liability partnership," except in the phrase "foreign limited liability partnership," means a partnership that has filed a statement of qualification under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(11): 48-1d-401; 48-1d-1405; 48-1d-701 "Partner" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(11)(a): 48-1d-401; 48-1d-1405 has become a partner in a partnership under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(11)(b): 48-1d-701 has not dissociated as a partner under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(12): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; 48-1d-1405 "Partnership" means an association of two or more persons to carry on as co-owners a business for profit formed under this chapter or that becomes subject to this chapter under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(13): 48-1d-106(1) "Partnership agreement" means the agreement, whether or not referred to as a partnership agreement, and whether oral, implied, in a record, or in any combination thereof, of all the partners of a partnership concerning the matters described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(14): "Partnership at will" means a partnership in which the partners have not agreed to remain partners until the expiration of a definite term or the completion of a particular undertaking.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(15): "Person" means an individual, business corporation, nonprofit corporation, partnership, limited partnership, limited liability company, limited cooperative association, unincorporated nonprofit association, statutory trust, business trust, common-law business trust, estate, trust, association, joint venture, public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality, or any other legal or commercial entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(16): "Principal office" means the principal executive office of a partnership or a foreign limited liability partnership, whether or not the office is located in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17): Title 58, Chapter 26a, Certified Public Accountant Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 3a, Architects Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 73, Chiropractic Physician Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 69, Dentist and Dental Hygienist Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 22, Professional Engineers and Professional Land Surveyors Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 71, Naturopathic Physician Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 31b, Nurse Practice Act; Chapter 44a, Nurse Midwife Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 16a, Utah Optometry Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 68, Utah Osteopathic Medical Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 17b, Pharmacy Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 67, Utah Medical Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 70a, Utah Physician Assistant Act; Title 58, Chapter 24b, Physical Therapy Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 5a, Podiatric Physician Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 61, Psychologist Licensing Act; Title 61, Chapter 2f, Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act; Title 58, Chapter 60, Part 2, Social Worker Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 60, Mental Health Professional Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 28, Veterinary Practice Act; Title 61, Chapter 2g, Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Act "Professional services" means a personal service provided by:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(a): Title 58, Chapter 26a, Certified Public Accountant Licensing Act a public accountant holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(b): Title 58, Chapter 3a, Architects Licensing Act an architect holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(c): an attorney granted the authority to practice law by the:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(c)(i): Utah Supreme Court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(c)(ii): one or more of the following that licenses or regulates the authority to practice law in a state or territory of the United States other than Utah:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(c)(ii)(A): a supreme court;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(c)(ii)(B): a court other than a supreme court;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(c)(ii)(C): an agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(c)(ii)(D): an instrumentality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(c)(ii)(E): a regulating board;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(d): Title 58, Chapter 73, Chiropractic Physician Practice Act a chiropractor holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(e): Title 58, Chapter 69, Dentist and Dental Hygienist Practice Act a doctor of dentistry holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(f): Title 58, Chapter 22, Professional Engineers and Professional Land Surveyors Licensing Act a professional engineer registered under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(g): Title 58, Chapter 71, Naturopathic Physician Practice Act a naturopath holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(h): Title 58, Chapter 31b, Nurse Practice Act; Chapter 44a, Nurse Midwife Practice Act a nurse licensed under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(i): Title 58, Chapter 16a, Utah Optometry Practice Act an optometrist holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(j): Title 58, Chapter 68, Utah Osteopathic Medical Practice Act an osteopathic physician or surgeon holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(k): Title 58, Chapter 17b, Pharmacy Practice Act a pharmacist holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(l): Title 58, Chapter 67, Utah Medical Practice Act a physician, surgeon, or doctor of medicine holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(m): Title 58, Chapter 70a, Utah Physician Assistant Act a physician assistant holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(n): Title 58, Chapter 24b, Physical Therapy Practice Act a physical therapist holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(o): Title 58, Chapter 5a, Podiatric Physician Licensing Act a podiatric physician holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(p): Title 58, Chapter 61, Psychologist Licensing Act a psychologist holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(q): Title 61, Chapter 2f, Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act a principal broker, associate broker, or sales agent holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(r): Title 58, Chapter 60, Part 2, Social Worker Licensing Act a clinical or certified social worker holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(s): Title 58, Chapter 60, Mental Health Professional Practice Act a mental health therapist holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(t): Title 58, Chapter 28, Veterinary Practice Act a veterinarian holding a license under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(17)(u): Title 61, Chapter 2g, Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Act an individual licensed, certified, or registered under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(18): "Property" means all property, whether real, personal, or mixed, or tangible or intangible, or any right or interest therein.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(19): "Record," used as a noun, means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(20): "Registered agent" means an agent of a limited liability partnership or foreign limited liability partnership which is authorized to receive service of any process, notice, or demand required or permitted by law to be served on the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(21): "Registered foreign limited liability partnership" means a foreign limited liability partnership that is registered to do business in this state pursuant to a statement of registration filed by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(22): "Sign" means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a record:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(22)(a): to execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(22)(b): to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic symbol, sound, or process.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(23): "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(24): "Transfer" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(24)(a): an assignment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(24)(b): a conveyance;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(24)(c): a sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(24)(d): a lease;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(24)(e): an encumbrance, including a mortgage or security interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(24)(f): a gift; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(24)(g): a transfer by operation of law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(25): "Transferable interest" means the right, as initially owned by a person in the person's capacity as a partner, to receive distributions from a partnership in accordance with the partnership agreement, whether or not the person remains a partner or continues to own any part of the right.  The term applies to any fraction of the interest, by whomever owned.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(26): "Transferee" means a person to which all or part of a transferable interest has been transferred, whether or not the transferor is a partner.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(27): "Tribal partnership" means a partnership:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(27)(a): formed under the law of a tribe; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(27)(b): that is at least 51% owned or controlled by the tribe under whose law the partnership is formed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-102(28): "Tribe" means a tribe, band, nation, pueblo, or other organized group or community of Indians, including an Alaska Native village, that is legally recognized as eligible for and is consistent with a special program, service, or entitlement provided by the United States to Indians because of their status as Indians.

----------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(1)(a): has actual knowledge of it; or

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(2)(a): has reason to know the fact from all the facts known to the person at the time in question; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(2)(b): (4)(b) is deemed to have notice of the fact under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(3): 48-1d-116(6) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(4): 48-1d-303(7); 48-1d-804; 48-1d-902(2)(b)(i); 48-1d-902(2)(b)(vi); Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication A person not a partner is deemed:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(4)(a): 48-1d-303(7) to know of a limitation on authority to transfer real property as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(4)(b): 48-1d-804; 48-1d-902(2)(b)(i); 48-1d-902(2)(b)(vi); Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication to have notice of:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(4)(b)(i): 48-1d-804 a partner's dissociation 90 days after a statement of dissociation under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(4)(b)(ii): 48-1d-902(2)(b)(i); 48-1d-902(2)(b)(vi); Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication a partnership's:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(4)(b)(ii)(A): 48-1d-902(2)(b)(i) dissolution 90 days after a statement of dissolution under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(4)(b)(ii)(C): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication participation in a merger, interest exchange, conversion, or domestication 90 days after a statement of merger, interest exchange, conversion, or domestication under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(4)(b)(ii)(D): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication abandonment of a merger, interest exchange, conversion, or domestication 90 days after a statement of abandonment of merger, interest exchange, conversion, or domestication under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-103(5): A partner's knowledge or notice of a fact relating to the partnership is effective immediately as knowledge of or notice to the partnership, except in the case of a fraud on the partnership committed by or with the consent of that partner.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-104 Governing law.
----------------------------------------------
The internal affairs of a partnership and the liability of a partner as a partner for the debts, obligations, or other liabilities of the partnership are governed by:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-104(1): in the case of a limited liability partnership, the law of this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-104(2): in the case of a partnership that is not a limited liability partnership, the law of the state of the jurisdiction in which the partnership has its principal office.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-105 Supplemental principles of law.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Unless displaced by particular provisions of this chapter, the principles of law and equity supplement this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-106(5)(b)(ii): the means to achieve the term's objective is unconscionable or against public policy.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-107 Partnership agreement -- Effect on partnership and person becoming partner -- Preformation agreement.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-107(1): A partnership is bound by and may enforce the partnership agreement, whether or not the partnership has itself manifested assent to the partnership agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-107(2): A person that becomes a partner of a partnership is deemed to assent to the partnership agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-107(3): Two or more persons intending to become the initial partners of a partnership may make an agreement providing that upon the formation of the partnership the agreement will become the partnership agreement.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108 Partnership agreement -- Effect on third parties and relationship to records effective on behalf of partnership.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(1): A partnership agreement may specify that its amendment requires the approval of a person that is not a party to the partnership agreement or the satisfaction of a condition.  An amendment is ineffective if its adoption does not include the required approval or satisfy the specified condition.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(2): 48-1d-604(2)(b); 48-1d-801 The obligations of a partnership and its partners to a person in the person's capacity as a transferee or person dissociated as a partner are governed by the partnership agreement.  Subject only to a court order issued under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(2)(a): is effective with regard to any debt, obligation, or other liability of the partnership or its partners to the person in the person's capacity as a transferee or person dissociated as a partner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(2)(b): 48-1d-801 is not effective to the extent the amendment:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(2)(b)(i): imposes a new debt, obligation, or other liability on the transferee or person dissociated as a partner; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(2)(b)(ii): 48-1d-801 prejudices the rights under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(3): 48-1d-106(3); (4)(b) If a record delivered by a partnership to the division for filing becomes effective under this chapter and contains a provision that would be ineffective under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(4): (3) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(4)(a): the partnership agreement prevails as to partners, persons dissociated as partners, and transferees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-108(4)(b): the record prevails as to other persons to the extent they reasonably rely on the record.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-109 Delivery of record.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-109(1): Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, permissible means of delivery of a record include delivery by hand, the United States Postal Service, commercial delivery service, and electronic transmission.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-109(2): Delivery to the division is effective only when a record is received by the division.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-110 Signing of records to be delivered for filing to division.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-110(1): (1)(b); (c); 48-1d-902(3); 48-1d-902(4); 48-1d-304 A record delivered to the division for filing pursuant to this chapter must be signed as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-110(1)(a): (1)(b); (c) Except as otherwise provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-110(1)(b): 48-1d-902(3); 48-1d-902(4) A record filed on behalf of a dissolved partnership that has no partner must be signed by the person winding up the partnership's activities and affairs under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-110(1)(c): 48-1d-304 A statement of denial by a person under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-110(1)(d): Any other record delivered on behalf of a person to the division for filing must be signed by that person.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-110(2): Any record filed under this chapter may be signed by an agent.  Whenever this chapter requires a particular individual to sign a record and the individual is deceased or incompetent, the record may be signed by a legal representative of the individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-110(3): A person that signs a record as an agent or legal representative thereby affirms as a fact that the person is authorized to sign the record.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-111 Signing and filing pursuant to judicial order.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-111(1): Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration If a person required by this chapter to sign a record or deliver a record to the division for filing under this chapter does not do so, any other person that is aggrieved may petition a court with jurisdiction under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-111(1)(a): the person to sign the record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-111(1)(b): the person to deliver the record to the division for filing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-111(1)(c): the division to file the record unsigned.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-111(2): (1) If a petitioner under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-111(3): (1)(c) A record filed under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112 Filing requirements.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(1): To be filed by the division pursuant to this chapter, a record must be received by the division, comply with this chapter, and satisfy the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(1)(a): The filing of the record must be required or permitted by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(1)(b): The record must be physically delivered in written form unless and to the extent the division permits electronic delivery of records.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(1)(c): The words in the record must be in English, and numbers must be in Arabic or Roman numerals, but the name of an entity need not be in English if written in English letters or Arabic or Roman numerals.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(1)(d): The record must be signed by a person authorized or required under this chapter to sign the record.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(1)(e): The record must state the name and capacity, if any, of each individual who signed it, either on behalf of the individual or the person authorized or required to sign the record, but need not contain a seal, attestation, acknowledgment, or verification.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(2): If law other than this chapter prohibits the disclosure by the division of information contained in a record delivered to the division for filing, the division shall accept the record if the record otherwise complies with this chapter but the division may redact the information.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(3): When a record is delivered to the division for filing, any fee required under this chapter and any fee, tax, interest, or penalty required to be paid under this chapter or law other than this chapter must be paid in a manner permitted by the division or by that law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-112(4): The division may require that a record delivered in written form be accompanied by an identical or conformed copy.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-113 Effective time and date.
--------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in SectionUtah Code Annotated § 48-1d-113(1): 48-1d-116 on the date and at the time of its filing by the division, as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-113(2): (1) on the date of filing and at the time specified in the record as its effective time, if later than the time under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-113(3): at a specified delayed effective time and date, which may not be more than 90 days after the date of filing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-113(4): if a delayed effective date is specified, but no time is specified, at 12:01 a.m. on the date specified, which may not be more than 90 days after the date of filing.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-114 Withdrawal of filed record before effectiveness.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-114(1): 48-1d-1024; 48-1d-1034; 48-1d-1044; 48-1d-1054 Except as otherwise provided in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-114(2): A statement of withdrawal must:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-114(2)(a): be signed by each person that signed the record being withdrawn, except as otherwise agreed by those persons;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-114(2)(b): identify the record to be withdrawn; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-114(2)(c): if signed by fewer than all the persons that signed the record being withdrawn, state that the record is withdrawn in accordance with the agreement of all the persons that signed the record.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-114(3): On filing by the division of a statement of withdrawal, the action or transaction evidenced by the original record does not take effect.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115 Correcting filed record.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(1): A person on whose behalf a filed record was delivered to the division for filing may correct the record if:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(1)(a): the record at the time of filing was inaccurate;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(1)(b): the record was defectively signed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(1)(c): the electronic transmission of the record to the division was defective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(2): To correct a filed record, a person on whose behalf the record was delivered to the division must deliver to the division for filing a statement of correction.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(3): A statement of correction:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(3)(a): may not state a delayed effective date;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(3)(b): must be signed by the person correcting the filed record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(3)(c): must identify the filed record to be corrected;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(3)(d): must specify the inaccuracy or defect to be corrected; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(3)(e): must correct the inaccuracy or defect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-115(4): 48-1d-103(4) A statement of correction is effective as of the effective date of the filed record that it corrects except for purposes of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116 Duty of division to file -- Review of refusal to file -- Transmission of information by division.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(1): The division shall file a record delivered to the division for filing which satisfies this chapter.  The duty of the division under this section is ministerial.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(2): When the division files a record, the division shall record it as filed on the date and at the time of its delivery.  After filing a record, the division shall deliver to the person that submitted the record a copy of the record with an acknowledgment of the date and time of filing and, in the case of a statement of denial, also to the partnership to which the statement pertains.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(3): If the division refuses to file a record, the division, not later than 15 business days after the record is delivered, shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(3)(a): return the record or notify the person that submitted the record of the refusal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(3)(b): provide a brief explanation in a record of the reason for the refusal.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(4): Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(4)(a): Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration If the division refuses to file a record, the person that submitted the record may petition a court with jurisdiction under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(4)(b): The record and the explanation of the division of the refusal to file must be attached to the petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(4)(c): The court may decide the matter in a summary proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(5): The filing of or refusal to file a record does not create a presumption that the information contained in the record is correct or incorrect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(6): 16-17-301 Except as otherwise provided by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(6)(a): in person to the person that submitted it;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(6)(b): to the address of the person's registered agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(6)(c): to the principal office of the person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-116(6)(d): to another address the person provides to the division for delivery.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-117(1): 48-1d-1101(6); 48-1d-111; 16-17-206; 48-1d-115 If a record delivered to the division for filing under this chapter and filed by the division contains inaccurate information, a person that suffers loss by reliance on the information may recover damages for the loss from:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-117(1)(a): a person that signed the record, or caused another to sign it on the person's behalf, and knew the information to be inaccurate at the time the record was signed; and

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-117(1)(b)(i): the record was delivered for filing on behalf of the partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-117(1)(b)(ii): 48-1d-1101(6); 48-1d-111; 16-17-206; 48-1d-115 the partner had notice of the inaccuracy for a reasonably sufficient time before the information was relied upon so that, before the reliance, the partner reasonably could have:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-117(1)(b)(ii)(C): 16-17-206; 48-1d-115 delivered to the division for filing a statement of change under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-117(2): An individual who signs a record authorized or required to be filed under this chapter affirms under penalty of perjury that the information stated in the record is accurate.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-118 Reservation of power to amend or repeal.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Legislature of this state has power to amend or repeal all or part of this chapter at any time, and all domestic and foreign limited liability partnerships subject to this chapter are governed by the amendment or repeal.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-201 Partnership as entity.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-201(1): A partnership is an entity distinct from its partners.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-201(2): 48-1d-1101 A partnership is the same entity regardless of whether the partnership has a statement of qualification in effect under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202 Formation of partnership.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(1): (2) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(2): An association formed under a statute other than this chapter, a predecessor statute, or a comparable statute of another jurisdiction is not a partnership under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3): In determining whether a partnership is formed, the following rules apply:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(a): Joint tenancy, tenancy in common, tenancy by the entireties, joint property, common property, or part ownership does not by itself establish a partnership, even if the co-owners share profits made by the use of the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(b): The sharing of gross returns does not by itself establish a partnership, even if the persons sharing them have a joint or common right or interest in property from which the returns are derived.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(c): A person who receives a share of the profits of a business is presumed to be a partner in the business, unless the profits were received in payment:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(c)(i): of a debt by installments or otherwise;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(c)(ii): for services as an independent contractor or of wages or other compensation to an employee;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(c)(iii): of rent;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(c)(iv): of an annuity or other retirement or health benefit to a deceased or retired partner or a beneficiary, representative, or designee of a deceased or retired partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(c)(v): of interest or other charge on a loan, even if the amount of payment varies with the profits of the business, including a direct or indirect present or future ownership of the collateral, or rights to income, proceeds, or increase in value derived from the collateral; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-202(3)(c)(vi): for the sale of the goodwill of a business or other property by installments or otherwise.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-203 Partnership property.
-----------------------------------------------------
Property acquired by a partnership is property of the partnership and not of the partners individually.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204 When property is partnership property.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204(1): Property is partnership property if acquired in the name of:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204(1)(a): the partnership; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204(1)(b): one or more partners with an indication in the instrument transferring title to the property of the person's capacity as a partner or of the existence of a partnership but without an indication of the name of the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204(2): Property is acquired in the name of the partnership by a transfer to:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204(2)(a): the partnership in its name; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204(2)(b): one or more partners in their capacity as partners in the partnership, if the name of the partnership is indicated in the instrument transferring title to the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204(3): Property is presumed to be partnership property if purchased with partnership assets, even if not acquired in the name of the partnership or of one or more partners with an indication in the instrument transferring title to the property of the person's capacity as a partner or of the existence of a partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-204(4): Property acquired in the name of one or more of the partners, without an indication in the instrument transferring title to the property of the person's capacity as a partner or of the existence of a partnership and without use of partnership assets, is presumed to be separate property, even if used for partnership purposes.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-301 Partner agent of partnership.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Subject to the effect of a statement of partnership authority under SectionUtah Code Annotated § 48-1d-301(1): Each partner is an agent of the partnership for the purpose of its activities and affairs.  An act of a partner, including the signing of an instrument in the partnership name, for apparently carrying on in the ordinary course the partnership's activities and affairs or activities and affairs of the kind carried on by the partnership binds the partnership, unless the partner did not have authority to act for the partnership in the particular matter and the person with which the partner was dealing knew, or had notice, that the partner lacked authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-301(2): An act of a partner, which is not apparently for carrying on in the ordinary course the partnership's activities and affairs or activities and affairs of the kind carried on by the partnership, binds the partnership only if the act was actually authorized by all the other partners.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-302 Transfer of partnership property.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-302(1): 48-1d-303 Partnership property may be transferred as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-302(1)(a): 48-1d-303 Subject to the effect of a statement of partnership authority under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-302(1)(b): Partnership property held in the name of one or more partners with an indication in the instrument transferring the property to them of their capacity as partners or of the existence of a partnership, but without an indication of the name of the partnership, may be transferred by an instrument of transfer executed by the persons in whose name the property is held.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-302(1)(c): Partnership property held in the name of one or more persons other than the partnership, without an indication in the instrument transferring the property to them of their capacity as partners or of the existence of a partnership, may be transferred by an instrument of transfer executed by the persons in whose name the property is held.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-302(2): 48-1d-301; (1)(a); (1)(b); (1)(c) A partnership may recover partnership property from a transferee only if it proves that execution of the instrument of initial transfer did not bind the partnership under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-302(2)(a): (1)(a); (1)(b) as to a subsequent transferee who gave value for property transferred under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-302(2)(b): (1)(c) as to a transferee who gave value for property transferred under Subsection

The person may execute a document in the name of the partnership to evidence vesting of the property in that person and may file or record the document.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-304 Statement of denial.
----------------------------------------------------
A person named in a filed statement of authority granting that person authority may deliver to the division for filing a statement of denial that:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-304(1): provides the name of the partnership and the caption of the statement of authority to which the statement of denial pertains; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-304(2): denies the grant of authority.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-305 Partnership liable for partner's actionable conduct.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-305(1): A partnership is liable for loss or injury caused to a person, or for a penalty incurred, as a result of a wrongful act or omission, or other actionable conduct, of a partner acting in the ordinary course of activities and affairs of the partnership or with the actual or apparent authority of the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-305(2): If, in the course of the partnership's activities and affairs or while acting with actual or apparent authority of the partnership, a partner receives or causes the partnership to receive money or property of a person not a partner, and the money or property is misapplied by a partner, the partnership is liable for the loss.

----------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-306(2): A person that becomes a partner is not personally liable for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the partnership incurred before the person became a partner.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-306(3): (3); 48-1d-1101(2) A debt, obligation, or other liability of a partnership incurred while the partnership is a limited liability partnership is solely the debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited liability partnership.  A partner is not personally liable, directly or indirectly, by way of contribution or otherwise, for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited liability partnership solely by reason of being or acting as a partner.  This Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-306(5): The cancellation or administrative revocation of a limited liability partnership's statement of qualification does not affect the limitation under this section on the liability of a partner for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the partnership incurred while the statement was in effect.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-307 Actions by and against partnership and partners.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-307(3): A judgment against a partnership is not by itself a judgment against a partner.  A judgment against a partnership may not be satisfied from a partner's assets unless there is also a judgment against the partner.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-307(4)(a): a judgment based on the same claim has been obtained against the partnership and a writ of execution on the judgment has been returned unsatisfied in whole or in part;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-307(4)(b): the partnership is a debtor in bankruptcy;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-307(4)(c): the partner has agreed that the creditor need not exhaust partnership assets;

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-307(4)(e): liability is imposed on the partner by law or contract independent of the existence of the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-307(5): 48-1d-308 This section applies to any partnership liability or obligation resulting from a representation by a partner or purported partner under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-308 Liability of purported partner.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-308(1): If a person, by words or conduct, purports to be a partner, or consents to being represented by another as a partner, in a partnership or with one or more persons not partners, the purported partner is liable to a person to whom the representation is made, if that person, relying on the representation, enters into a transaction with the actual or purported partnership.  If the representation, either by the purported partner or by a person with the purported partner's consent, is made in a public manner, the purported partner is liable to a person who relies upon the purported partnership even if the purported partner is not aware of being held out as a partner to the claimant.  If partnership liability results, the purported partner is liable with respect to that liability as if the purported partner were a partner.  If no partnership liability results, the purported partner is liable with respect to that liability jointly and severally with any other person consenting to the representation.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-308(2): If a person is thus represented to be a partner in an existing partnership, or with one or more persons not partners, the purported partner is an agent of persons consenting to the representation to bind them to the same extent and in the same manner as if the purported partner were a partner, with respect to persons who enter into transactions in reliance upon the representation.  If all the partners of the existing partnership consent to the representation, a partnership act or obligation results.  If fewer than all the partners of the existing partnership consent to the representation, the person acting and the partners consenting to the representation are jointly and severally liable.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-308(3): A person is not liable as a partner merely because the person is named by another in a statement of partnership authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-308(4): A person does not continue to be liable as a partner merely because of a failure to file a statement of dissociation or to amend a statement of partnership authority to indicate the partner's dissociation from the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-308(5): (1); (2) Except as otherwise provided in Subsections


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401 Becoming partner.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401(1): 48-1d-202(1) Upon formation of a partnership, a person becomes a partner under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401(2): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication After formation of a partnership, a person becomes a partner:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401(2)(a): as provided in the partnership agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401(2)(b): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication as a result of a transaction effective under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401(2)(c): with the consent of all the partners.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401(3): A person may become a partner without either:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401(3)(a): acquiring a transferable interest; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-401(3)(b): making or being obligated to make a contribution to the partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-402 Management rights of partners.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-402(1): Each partner has equal rights in the management and conduct of the partnership's activities and affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-402(2): A partner may use or possess partnership property only on behalf of the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-402(3): A partner is not entitled to remuneration for services performed for the partnership, except for reasonable compensation for services rendered in winding up the activities and affairs of the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-402(4): A difference arising among partners as to a matter in the ordinary course of the activities of the partnership shall be decided by a majority of the partners.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-402(5): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication An act outside the ordinary course of the activities and affairs of the partnership may be undertaken only with the consent of all partners.  An act outside the ordinary course of business of a partnership, an amendment to the partnership agreement, and the approval of a transaction under


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-403 Rights of partners and person dissociated as partner to information.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-403(1): A partnership shall keep its books and records, if any, at its principal office.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-403(2): On reasonable notice, a partner may inspect and copy during regular business hours, at a reasonable location specified by the partnership, any record maintained by the partnership regarding the partnership's activities, affairs, financial condition, and other circumstances, to the extent the information is material to the partner's rights and duties under the partnership agreement or this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-405(2)(a)(i): in the conduct or winding up of the partnership's activities and affairs;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-405(2)(a)(ii): from a use by the partner of the partnership's property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-405(2)(a)(iii): from the appropriation of a partnership opportunity;

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-405(2)(c): to refrain from competing with the partnership in the conduct of the partnership's activities and affairs before the dissolution of the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-405(3): The duty of care of a partner in the conduct or winding up of the partnership's activities and affairs is to refrain from engaging in grossly negligent or reckless conduct, intentional misconduct, or a knowing violation of law.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-406 Actions by partnership and partners.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-406(1): A partnership may maintain an action against a partner for a breach of the partnership agreement, or for the violation of a duty to the partnership, causing harm to the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-406(2): A partner may maintain an action against the partnership or another partner for legal or equitable relief, with or without an accounting as to the partnership's activities and affairs, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-406(2)(a): enforce the partner's rights under the partnership agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-406(2)(b): enforce the partner's rights under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-406(2)(c): enforce the rights and otherwise protect the interests of the partner, including rights and interests arising independently of the partnership relationship.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-406(3): The accrual of, and any time limitation on, a right of action for a remedy under this section is governed by other law.  A right to an accounting upon a dissolution and winding up does not revive a claim barred by law.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-407 Continuation of partnership beyond definite term or particular undertaking.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-407(1): If a partnership for a definite term or particular undertaking is continued, without an express agreement, after the expiration of the term or completion of the undertaking, the rights and duties of the partners remain the same as they were at the expiration or completion, so far as is consistent with a partnership at will.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-407(2): If the partners, or those of them who habitually acted in the business during the term or undertaking, continue the business without any settlement or liquidation of the partnership, they are presumed to have agreed that the partnership will continue.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-501 Form of contribution.
-----------------------------------------------------
A contribution may consist of property transferred to, services performed for, or other benefit provided to the partnership or an agreement to transfer property to, perform services for, or provide another benefit to the partnership.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-502 Liability for contribution.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-502(1): A person's obligation to make a contribution to a partnership is not excused by the person's death, disability, dissolution, or other inability to perform personally.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-502(2): If a person does not fulfill an obligation to make a contribution other than money, the person is obligated at the option of the partnership to contribute money equal to the value of the part of the contribution which has not been made.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-502(3): (1); (3) The obligation of a person to make a contribution may be compromised only by consent of all partners.  If a creditor of a limited liability partnership extends credit or otherwise acts in reliance on an obligation described in Subsection

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-503(1): 48-1d-603; 48-1d-604 Any distributions made by a partnership before its dissolution and winding up must be in equal shares among partners, except to the extent necessary to comply with a transfer effective under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-503(2): A person has a right to a distribution before the dissolution and winding up of a partnership only if the partnership decides to make an interim distribution.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-503(3): 48-1d-906 A person does not have a right to demand or receive a distribution from a partnership in any form other than money.  Except as otherwise provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-503(4): If a partner or transferee becomes entitled to receive a distribution, the partner or transferee has the status of, and is entitled to all remedies available to, a creditor of the partnership with respect to the distribution.  However, the partnership's obligation to make a distribution is subject to offset for any amount owed to the partnership by the partner or a person dissociated as partner on whose account the distribution is made.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-601 Partner not co-owner of partnership property.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
A partner is not a co-owner of partnership property and has no interest in partnership property which can be transferred, either voluntarily or involuntarily.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-602 Nature of transferable interest.
----------------------------------------------------------------
A transferable interest is personal property.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604 Charging order.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(1): On application by a judgment creditor of a partner or transferee, a court may enter a charging order against the transferable interest of the judgment debtor for the unsatisfied amount of the judgment.  A charging order constitutes a lien on a judgment debtor's transferable interest and, after the partnership has been served with the charging order, requires the partnership to pay over to the person to which the charging order was issued any distribution that otherwise would be paid to the judgment debtor.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(2): (1) To the extent necessary to effectuate the collection of distributions pursuant to a charging order in effect under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(2)(a): appoint a receiver of the distributions subject to the charging order, with the power to make all inquiries the judgment debtor might have made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(2)(b): make all other orders necessary to give effect to the charging order.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(3): 48-1d-603 Upon a showing that distributions under a charging order will not pay the judgment debt within a reasonable time, the court may foreclose the lien and order the sale of the transferable interest.  The purchaser at the foreclosure sale obtains only the transferable interest, does not thereby become a partner, and is subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(4): (3); (1) At any time before foreclosure under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(5): (3) At any time before foreclosure under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(6): This chapter does not deprive any partner or transferee of the benefit of any exemption law applicable to the transferable interest of the partner or transferee.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-604(7): This section provides the exclusive remedy by which a person seeking to enforce a judgment against a partner or transferee, in the capacity of judgment creditor, may satisfy the judgment from the judgment debtor's transferable interest.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701 Events causing dissociation.
------------------------------------------------------------
A person is dissociated as a partner when:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(1): the partnership has notice of the person's express will to withdraw as a partner, but, if the person specified a withdrawal date later than the date the partnership had notice, on that later date;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(2): an event stated in the partnership agreement as causing the person's dissociation occurs;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(3): the person is expelled as a partner pursuant to the partnership agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4): 48-1d-604 the person is expelled as a partner by the unanimous vote or consent of the other partners if:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4)(a): it is unlawful to carry on the partnership's activities and affairs with the person as a partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4)(b): 48-1d-604 there has been a transfer of all of the person's transferable interest in the partnership, other than:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4)(b)(i): a transfer for security purposes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4)(b)(ii): 48-1d-604 a charging order in effect under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4)(c): the person is a corporation and:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4)(c)(i): the partnership notifies the person that it will be expelled as a partner because the person has filed a statement of dissolution or the equivalent, its charter has been revoked, or its right to conduct business has been suspended by the jurisdiction of its incorporation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4)(c)(ii): not later than 90 days after the notification, the statement of dissolution or the equivalent has not been revoked or the charter or right to conduct business has not been reinstated; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(4)(d): the person is an unincorporated entity that has been dissolved and whose business is being wound up;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(5): 48-1d-405 on application by the partnership or another partner, the person is expelled as a partner by judicial order because the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(5)(a): has engaged or is engaging in wrongful conduct that has affected adversely and materially, or will affect adversely and materially, the partnership's activities and affairs;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(5)(b): 48-1d-405 has committed willfully or persistently, or is committing willfully or persistently, a material breach of the partnership agreement or a duty or obligation under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(5)(c): engaged or is engaging in conduct relating to the partnership's activities and affairs which makes it not reasonably practicable to carry on the partnership's activities and affairs with the person as a partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(6): in the case of an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(6)(a): the individual dies;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(6)(b): a guardian or general conservator for the individual is appointed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(6)(c): a court orders that the individual has otherwise become incapable of performing the individual's duties as a partner under this chapter or the partnership agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(7): the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(7)(a): becomes a debtor in bankruptcy;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(7)(b): executes an assignment for the benefit of creditors; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(7)(c): seeks, consents to, or acquiesces in the appointment of a trustee, receiver, or liquidator of the person or of all, or substantially all, of the person's property;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(8): in the case of a person that is a testamentary or inter vivos trust or is acting as a partner by virtue of being a trustee of such a trust, the trust's entire transferable interest in the partnership is distributed;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(9): in the case of a person that is an estate or is acting as a partner by virtue of being a personal representative of an estate, the estate's entire transferable interest in the partnership is distributed, but not merely by reason of the substitution of a successor personal representative;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(10): in the case of a person that is not an individual, corporation, unincorporated entity, trust, or estate, the existence of the person terminates;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(11): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication the partnership participates in a merger under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(11)(a): the partnership is not the surviving entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(11)(b): otherwise as a result of the merger, the person ceases to be a partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(12): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication the partnership participates in an interest exchange under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(13): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication the partnership participates in a conversion under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(14): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication the partnership participates in a domestication under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-701(15): the partnership dissolves and completes winding up.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702 Power to dissociate as partner -- Wrongful dissociation.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702(1): 48-1d-701(1) A person has the power to dissociate as a partner at any time, rightfully or wrongfully, by withdrawing as a partner by express will under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702(2): 48-1d-701(6); (10); 48-1d-701(5); 48-1d-701(7) A person's dissociation as a partner is wrongful only if the dissociation:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702(2)(a): is in breach of an express provision of the partnership agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702(2)(b): 48-1d-701(6); (10); 48-1d-701(5); 48-1d-701(7) in the case of a partnership for a definite term or particular undertaking, occurs before the expiration of the term or the completion of the undertaking and:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702(2)(b)(i): 48-1d-701(6); (10) the person withdraws by express will, unless the withdrawal follows not later than 90 days after another person's dissociation by death or otherwise under Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702(2)(b)(iii): 48-1d-701(7) the person is dissociated under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702(2)(b)(iv): in the case of a person that is not a trust other than a business trust, an estate, an individual, or a trust other than a business trust, the person is expelled or otherwise dissociated because it willfully dissolved or terminated.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-702(3): A person that wrongfully dissociates is liable to the partnership and to the other partners for damages caused by the dissociation.  The liability is in addition to any debt, obligation, or other liability of the partner to the partnership or the other partners.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803 Liability of person dissociated as partner to other persons.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803(1): (2) A person's dissociation as a partner does not of itself discharge the person's liability as a partner for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the partnership incurred before dissociation.  Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803(2): A person that has dissociated as a partner without the dissociation resulting in a dissolution and winding up of the partnership's activities and affairs is liable on a transaction entered into by the partnership after the dissociation only if:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803(2)(a): a partner would be liable on the transaction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803(2)(b): at the time the other party enters into the transaction:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803(2)(b)(i): less than two years has passed since the dissociation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803(2)(b)(ii): the other party does not have knowledge or notice of the dissociation and reasonably believes that the person is a partner.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803(3): By agreement with a creditor of a partnership and the partnership, a person dissociated as a partner may be released from liability for an obligation of the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-803(4): A person dissociated as a partner is released from liability for an obligation of the partnership if the partnership's creditor, with knowledge or notice of the person's dissociation but without the person's consent, agrees to a material alteration in the nature or time of payment of the obligation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-804 Statement of dissociation.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-804(1): A person dissociated as a partner or the partnership may file a statement of dissociation stating the name of the partnership and that the partner is dissociated from the partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-804(2): 48-1d-303(4); (5) A statement of dissociation is a limitation on the authority of a person dissociated as a partner for the purposes of Subsections


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-805 Continued use of partnership name.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Continued use of a partnership name, or name of a person dissociated as a partner as part of the partnership name, by partners continuing the business does not of itself make the person dissociated as a partner liable for an obligation of the partners or the partnership continuing the business.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901 Events causing dissolution.
-----------------------------------------------------------
A partnership is dissolved, and the partnership's activities and affairs must be wound up, upon the occurrence of any of the following:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(1): 48-1d-701(2); (10) in a partnership at will, the partnership has notice of a person's express will to withdraw as a partner, other than a partner that has dissociated under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(2): 48-1d-701(6); (10); 48-1d-702(2); 48-1d-702(2)(b)(i) in a partnership for a definite term or particular undertaking:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(2)(a): 48-1d-701(6); (10); 48-1d-702(2); 48-1d-702(2)(b)(i) within 90 days after a person's dissociation by death or otherwise under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(2)(b): the express consent of all the partners to wind up the partnership's activities and affairs; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(2)(c): the expiration of the term or the completion of the undertaking;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(3): an event or circumstance that the partnership agreement states causes dissolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(4): upon a petition brought by a partner, the entry of a court order dissolving the partnership on the ground that:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(4)(a): the conduct of all or substantially all the partnership's activities and affairs is unlawful;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(4)(b): the economic purpose of the partnership is likely to be unreasonably frustrated;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(4)(c): another partner has engaged in conduct relating to the partnership's activities and affairs which makes it not reasonably practicable to carry on the business in partnership with that partner; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(4)(d): it is not otherwise reasonably practicable to carry on the partnership's activities and affairs in conformity with the partnership agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(5): upon a petition brought by a transferee, the entry of a court order dissolving the partnership on the ground that it is equitable to wind up the partnership's activities and affairs:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(5)(a): after the expiration of the term or completion of the undertaking, if the partnership was for a definite term or particular undertaking at the time of the transfer or entry of the charging order that gave rise to the transfer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(5)(b): at any time, if the partnership was a partnership at will at the time of the transfer or entry of the charging order that gave rise to the transfer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-901(6): the passage of 90 consecutive days during which the partnership does not have at least two partners.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902 Winding up.
-------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(1): 48-1d-903
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(1)(a): A dissolved partnership shall wind up the partnership's activities and affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(1)(b): 48-1d-903 Except as otherwise provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2): In winding up a partnership's activities and affairs, the partnership:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(a): shall discharge the partnership's debts, obligations, and other liabilities, settle and close the partnership's activities and affairs, and marshal and distribute the assets of the partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(b): may:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(b)(i): deliver to the division for filing a statement of dissolution stating the name of the partnership and that the partnership is dissolved;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(b)(ii): preserve the partnership's activities and affairs and property as a going concern for a reasonable time;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(b)(iii): prosecute and defend actions and proceedings, whether civil, criminal, or administrative;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(b)(iv): transfer the partnership's property;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(b)(v): settle disputes by mediation or arbitration;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(b)(vi): deliver to the division for filing a statement of termination stating the name of the partnership and that the partnership is terminated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(2)(b)(vii): perform other acts necessary or appropriate to the winding up.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(3): A person whose dissociation as a partner resulted in dissolution may participate in winding up as if still a partner, unless the dissociation was wrongful.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(4): (3); (4); 48-1d-904 If a dissolved partnership does not have a partner and no person has the right to participate in winding up under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(5): (3); (4) Upon a petition brought by any partner or person entitled under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(5)(a): (4) the partnership does not have a partner, and within a reasonable time following the dissolution no person has been appointed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-902(5)(b): the applicant establishes other good cause.
