Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
In this part:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(1): "Acquired entity" means the entity, all of one or more classes or series of interests in which are acquired in an interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(2): "Acquiring entity" means the entity that acquires all of one or more classes or series of interests of the acquired entity in an interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(3): 48-1d-1041; 48-1d-1046 "Conversion" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(4): "Converted entity" means the converting entity as it continues in existence after a conversion.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(5): 48-1d-1043 "Converting entity" means the domestic entity that approves a plan of conversion pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(6): "Distributional interest" means the right under an unincorporated entity's organic law and organic rules to receive distributions from the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(7): "Domestic," with respect to an entity, means governed as to its internal affairs by the law of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(8): "Domesticated limited liability partnership" means a domesticating limited liability partnership as it continues in existence after a domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(9): 48-1d-1053 "Domesticating limited liability partnership" means a domestic limited liability partnership that approves a plan of domestication pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(10): 48-1d-1051; 48-1d-1056 "Domestication" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11): 48-1d-202(3) "Entity":
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a): means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(i): a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(ii): a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(iii): a general partnership, including a limited liability partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(iv): a limited partnership, including a limited liability limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(v): a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(vi): a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(vii): an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(viii): a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(ix): any other person that has:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(ix)(A): a legal existence separate from any interest holder of that person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(a)(ix)(B): the power to acquire an interest in real property in its own name; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(b): 48-1d-202(3) does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(b)(i): an individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(b)(ii): a trust with a predominantly donative purpose, or a charitable trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(b)(iii): 48-1d-202(3) an association or relationship that is not a partnership solely by reason of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(b)(iv): a decedent's estate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(11)(b)(v): a government or a governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(12): "Filing entity" means an entity whose formation requires the filing of a public organic record.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(13): "Foreign," with respect to an entity, means an entity governed as to its internal affairs by the law of a jurisdiction other than this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(14): "Governance interest" means a right under the organic law or organic rules of an unincorporated entity, other than as a governor, agent, assignee, or proxy, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(14)(a): receive or demand access to information concerning, or the books and records of, the entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(14)(b): vote for or consent to the election of the governors of the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(14)(c): receive notice of or vote on or consent to an issue involving the internal affairs of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15): "Governor" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(a): a director of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(b): a director or trustee of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(c): a general partner of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(d): a general partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(e): a manager of a manager-managed limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(f): a member of a member-managed limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(g): a director of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(h): a manager of an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(i): a trustee of a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(15)(j): any other person under whose authority the powers of an entity are exercised and under whose direction the activities and affairs of the entity are managed pursuant to the organic law and organic rules of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16): "Interest" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(a): a share in a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(b): a membership in a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(c): a partnership interest in a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(d): a partnership interest in a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(e): a membership interest in a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(f): a member's interest in a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(g): a membership in an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(h): a beneficial interest in a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(16)(i): a governance interest or distributional interest in any other type of unincorporated entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(17): 48-1d-1031; 48-1d-1036 "Interest exchange" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18): "Interest holder" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(a): a shareholder of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(b): a member of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(c): a general partner of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(d): a general partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(e): a limited partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(f): a member of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(g): a member of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(h): a member of an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(i): a beneficiary or beneficial owner of a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(18)(j): any other direct holder of an interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(19): "Interest holder liability" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(19)(a): personal liability for a liability of an entity which is imposed on a person:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(19)(a)(i): solely by reason of the status of the person as an interest holder; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(19)(a)(ii): by the organic rules of the entity which make one or more specified interest holders or categories of interest holders liable in their capacity as interest holders for all or specified liabilities of the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(19)(b): an obligation of an interest holder under the organic rules of an entity to contribute to the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(20): "Jurisdiction of formation" means the jurisdiction whose law includes the organic law of an entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(21): 48-1d-1021; 48-1d-1026 "Merger" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(22): "Merging entity" means an entity that is a party to a merger and exists immediately before the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(23): "Organic law" means the law of an entity's jurisdiction of formation governing the internal affairs of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(24): "Organic rules" means the public organic record and private organic rules of an entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(25): "Plan" means a plan of merger, plan of interest exchange, plan of conversion, or plan of domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(26): 48-1d-1042 "Plan of conversion" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(27): 48-1d-1052 "Plan of domestication" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(28): 48-1d-1032 "Plan of interest exchange" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(29): 48-1d-1022 "Plan of merger" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30): "Private organic rules" means the rules, whether or not in a record, that govern the internal affairs of an entity, are binding on all its interest holders, and are not part of its public organic record, if any.  The term includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30)(a): the bylaws of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30)(b): the bylaws of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30)(c): the partnership agreement of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30)(d): the partnership agreement of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30)(e): the operating agreement of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30)(f): the bylaws of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30)(g): the governing principles of an unincorporated nonprofit association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(30)(h): the trust instrument of a statutory trust or similar rules of a business trust or common-law business trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(31): "Protected agreement" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(31)(a): a record evidencing indebtedness and any related agreement in effect on January 1, 2014;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(31)(b): an agreement that is binding on an entity on January 1, 2014;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(31)(c): the organic rules of an entity in effect on January 1, 2014; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(31)(d): an agreement that is binding on any of the governors or interest holders of an entity on January 1, 2014.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(32): "Public organic record" means the record the filing of which by the division is required to form an entity and any amendment to or restatement of that record.  The term includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(32)(a): the articles of incorporation of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(32)(b): the articles of incorporation of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(32)(c): the certificate of limited partnership of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(32)(d): the certificate of organization of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(32)(e): the articles of organization of a limited cooperative association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(32)(f): the certificate of trust of a statutory trust or similar record of a business trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(33): "Registered foreign entity" means a foreign entity that is registered to do business in this state pursuant to a record filed by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(34): 48-1d-1045 "Statement of conversion" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(35): 48-1d-1055 "Statement of domestication" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(36): 48-1d-1035 "Statement of interest exchange" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(37): 48-1d-1025 "Statement of merger" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(38): "Surviving entity" means an entity that continues in existence after or is created by a merger.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(39): "Type of entity" means a generic form of entity:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(39)(a): recognized at common law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1001(39)(b): formed under an organic law, whether or not some entities formed under that organic law are subject to provisions of that law that create different categories of the form of entity.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1002 Relationship of part to other laws.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
This part does not authorize an act prohibited by, and does not affect the application or requirements of, law other than this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1003 Required notice or approval.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1003(1): A domestic or foreign entity that is required to give notice to, or obtain the approval of, a governmental agency or officer of this state to be a party to a merger must give the notice or obtain the approval to be a party to an interest exchange, conversion, or domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1003(2): Property held for a charitable purpose under the law of this state by a domestic or foreign entity immediately before a transaction under this part becomes effective may not, as a result of the transaction, be diverted from the objects for which it was donated, granted, devised, or otherwise transferred unless, to the extent required by or pursuant to the law of this state concerning cy pres or other law dealing with nondiversion of charitable assets, the entity obtains a court order specifying the disposition of the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1003(3): A bequest, devise, gift, grant, or promise contained in a will or other instrument of donation, subscription, or conveyance that is made to a merging entity that is not the surviving entity and that takes effect or remains payable after the merger inures to the surviving entity.  A trust obligation that would govern property if transferred to the nonsurviving entity applies to property that is transferred to the surviving entity under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1004 Status of filings.
---------------------------------------------------
A filing under this part signed by a domestic entity becomes part of the public organic record of the entity if the entity's organic law provides that similar filings under that law become part of the public organic record of the entity.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1005 Nonexclusivity.
------------------------------------------------
The fact that a transaction under this part produces a certain result does not preclude the same result from being accomplished in any other manner permitted by law other than this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1006 Reference to external facts.
-------------------------------------------------------------
A plan may refer to facts ascertainable outside the plan if the manner in which the facts will operate upon the plan is specified in the plan.  The facts may include the occurrence of an event or a determination or action by a person, whether or not the event, determination, or action is within the control of a party to the transaction.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1007 Alternative means of approval of transactions.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or organic rules of a domestic entity, approval of a transaction under this part by the unanimous vote or consent of its interest holders satisfies the requirements of this part for approval of the transaction.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1008 Appraisal rights.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1008(1): An interest holder of a domestic merging, acquired, converting, or domesticating entity is entitled to appraisal rights in connection with the transaction if the interest holder would have been entitled to appraisal rights under the entity's organic law in connection with a merger in which the interest of the interest holder was changed, converted, or exchanged unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1008(1)(a): the organic law permits the organic rules to limit the availability of appraisal rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1008(1)(b): the organic rules provide such a limit.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1008(2): An interest holder of a domestic merging, acquired, converting, or domesticating entity is entitled to contractual appraisal rights in connection with a transaction under this part to the extent provided in:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1008(2)(a): the entity's organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1008(2)(b): the plan.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1021 Merger authorized.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1021(1): 48-1d-1021; 48-1d-1026 By complying with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1021(1)(a): one or more domestic partnerships may merge with one or more domestic or foreign entities into a domestic or foreign surviving entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1021(1)(b): two or more foreign entities may merge into a domestic partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1021(2): 48-1d-1021; 48-1d-1026; 48-1d-1021; 48-1d-1026 By complying with the provisions of Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022 Plan of merger.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(1): 48-1d-1021; 48-1d-1026 A domestic partnership may become a party to a merger under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(1)(a): as to each merging entity, its name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(1)(b): if the surviving entity is to be created in the merger, a statement to that effect and the entity's name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(1)(c): the manner of converting the interests in each party to the merger into interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(1)(d): if the surviving entity exists before the merger, any proposed amendments to its public organic record, if any, or to its private organic rules that are, or are proposed to be, in a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(1)(e): if the surviving entity is to be created in the merger, its proposed public organic record, if any, and the full text of its private organic rules that are proposed to be in a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(1)(f): the other terms and conditions of the merger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(1)(g): any other provision required by the law of a merging entity's jurisdiction of formation or the organic rules of a merging entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1022(2): (1) In addition to the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1023 Approval of merger.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1023(1): A plan of merger is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1023(1)(a): by a domestic merging partnership, by all the partners of the partnership entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1023(1)(b): in a record, by each partner of a domestic merging partnership that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the merger becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1023(1)(b)(i): the partnership agreement of the partnership provides in a record for the approval of a merger in which some or all of its partners become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the partners; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1023(1)(b)(ii): the partner consented in a record to or voted for that provision of the partnership agreement or became a partner after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1023(2): A merger involving a domestic merging entity that is not a partnership is not effective unless the merger is approved by that entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1023(3): A merger involving a foreign merging entity is not effective unless the merger is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024 Amendment or abandonment of plan of merger.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(1): A plan of merger may be amended only with the consent of each party to the plan, except as otherwise provided in the plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(2): A domestic merging partnership may approve an amendment of a plan of merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(2)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(2)(b): by the partners in the manner provided in the plan, but a partner that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the merger is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(2)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by the interest holders of any party to the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(2)(b)(ii): the public organic record, if any, or private organic rules of the surviving entity that will be in effect immediately after the merger becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the interest holders of the surviving entity under its organic law or organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(2)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the partner in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(3): After a plan of merger has been approved and before a statement of merger becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic merging partnership may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(4): If a plan of merger is abandoned after a statement of merger has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement of merger becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by a party to the plan, must be delivered to the division for filing before the statement of merger becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the merger is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(4)(a): the name of each party to the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(4)(b): the date on which the statement of merger was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1024(4)(c): a statement that the merger has been abandoned in accordance with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025 Statement of merger.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(1): A statement of merger must be signed by each merging entity and delivered to the division for filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(2): 48-1d-1021; 48-1d-1026; 48-1d-1026(5) A statement of merger must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(2)(a): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of each merging entity that is not the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(2)(b): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(2)(c): 48-1d-1021; 48-1d-1026 a statement that the merger was approved by each domestic merging entity, if any, in accordance with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(2)(d): if the surviving entity exists before the merger and is a domestic filing entity, any amendment to its public organic record approved as part of the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(2)(e): if the surviving entity is created by the merger and is a domestic filing entity, its public organic record, as an attachment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(2)(f): if the surviving entity is created by the merger and is a domestic limited liability partnership, its statement of qualification, as an attachment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(2)(g): 48-1d-1026(5) if the surviving entity is a foreign entity that is not a registered foreign entity, a mailing address to which the division may send any process served on the division pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(3): (2) In addition to the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(4): If the surviving entity is a domestic entity, its public organic record, if any, must satisfy the requirements of the law of this state, except that the public organic record does not need to be signed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1025(5): (2); (5); (5) A plan of merger that is signed by all the merging entities and meets all the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026 Effect of merger.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1): 48-1d-1008 When a merger becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(a): the surviving entity continues or comes into existence;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(b): each merging entity that is not the surviving entity ceases to exist;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(c): all property of each merging entity vests in the surviving entity without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(d): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of each merging entity are debts, obligations, and liabilities of the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(e): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of merger, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of each merging entity vest in the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(f): if the surviving entity exists before the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(f)(i): all its property continues to be vested in it without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(f)(ii): it remains subject to all its debts, obligations, and other liabilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(f)(iii): all its rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes continue to be vested in it;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(g): the name of the surviving entity may be substituted for the name of any merging entity that is a party to any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(h): if the surviving entity exists before the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(h)(i): its public organic record, if any, is amended as provided in the statement of merger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(h)(ii): its private organic rules that are to be in a record, if any, are amended to the extent provided in the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(i): if the surviving entity is created by the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(i)(i): its public organic record, if any, is effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(i)(ii): its private organic rules are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(1)(j): 48-1d-1008 the interests in each merging entity which are to be converted in the merger are converted, and the interest holders of those interests are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of merger and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(2): Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or organic rules of a merging entity, the merger does not give rise to any rights that an interest holder, governor, or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the merging entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(3): When a merger becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to any of the merging entities and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the merger has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of that entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(4): (4)(a); (4)(a) When a merger becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic merging entity with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(4)(a): The merger does not discharge any interest holder liability under the organic law of the domestic merging entity to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the merger became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(4)(b): The person does not have interest holder liability under the organic law of the domestic merging entity for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(4)(c): (4)(a) The organic law of the domestic merging entity continues to apply to the release, collection, or discharge of any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(4)(d): (4)(a) The person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the organic rules of the domestic merging entity with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(5): 16-17-301 When a merger becomes effective, a foreign entity that is the surviving entity may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any debts, obligations, or other liabilities of a domestic merging entity as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1026(6): When a merger becomes effective, the registration to do business in this state of any foreign merging entity that is not the surviving entity is canceled.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1031 Interest exchange authorized.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1031(1): 48-1d-1031; 48-1d-1036 By complying with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1031(1)(a): a domestic partnership may acquire all of one or more classes or series of interests of another domestic or foreign entity in exchange for interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1031(1)(b): all of one or more classes or series of interests of a domestic partnership may be acquired by another domestic or foreign entity in exchange for interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1031(2): 48-1d-1031; 48-1d-1036; 48-1d-1031; 48-1d-1036 By complying with the provisions of Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1031(3): If a protected agreement contains a provision that applies to a merger of a domestic partnership but does not refer to an interest exchange, the provision applies to an interest exchange in which the domestic partnership is the acquired entity as if the interest exchange were a merger until the provision is amended after January 1, 2014.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1032 Plan of interest exchange.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1032(1): 48-1d-1031; 48-1d-1036 A domestic partnership may be the acquired entity in an interest exchange under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1032(1)(a): the name of the acquired entity;

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1032(1)(c): the manner of converting the interests in the acquired entity into interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1032(1)(d): any proposed amendments to the partnership agreement that are, or are proposed to be, in a record of the acquired entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1032(1)(e): the other terms and conditions of the interest exchange; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1032(1)(f): any other provision required by the law of this state or the partnership agreement of the acquired entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1032(2): (1) In addition to the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033 Approval of interest exchange.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033(1): A plan of interest exchange is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033(1)(a): by all the partners of a domestic acquired partnership entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033(1)(b): in a record, by each partner of the domestic acquired partnership that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the interest exchange becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033(1)(b)(i): the partnership agreement of the partnership provides in a record for the approval of an interest exchange or a merger in which some or all its partners become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the partners; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033(1)(b)(ii): the partner consented in a record to or voted for that provision of the partnership agreement or became a partner after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033(2): An interest exchange involving a domestic acquired entity that is not a partnership is not effective unless it is approved by the domestic entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033(3): An interest exchange involving a foreign acquired entity is not effective unless it is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1033(4): Except as otherwise provided in its organic law or organic rules, the interest holders of the acquiring entity are not required to approve the interest exchange.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034 Amendment or abandonment of plan of interest exchange.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(1): A plan of interest exchange may be amended only with the consent of each party to the plan, except as otherwise provided in the plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(2): A domestic acquired partnership may approve an amendment of a plan of interest exchange:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(2)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(2)(b): by the partners of the acquired partnership in the manner provided in the plan, but a partner that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the interest exchange is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(2)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by any of the partners of the acquired partnership under the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(2)(b)(ii): the partnership agreement of the acquired partnership that will be in effect immediately after the interest exchange becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the partners of the acquired partnership under this chapter or the partnership agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(2)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the partner in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(3): After a plan of interest exchange has been approved and before a statement of interest exchange becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic acquired partnership may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(4): If a plan of interest exchange is abandoned after a statement of interest exchange has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by the acquired partnership, must be delivered to the division for filing before the statement of interest exchange becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the interest exchange is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(4)(a): the name of the acquired partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(4)(b): the date on which the statement of interest exchange was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1034(4)(c): a statement that the interest exchange has been abandoned in accordance with this section.

----------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036 Effect of interest exchange.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(1): 48-1d-1008 When an interest exchange in which the acquired entity is a domestic partnership becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(1)(a): 48-1d-1008 the interests in the domestic acquired partnership that are the subject of the interest exchange cease to exist or are converted or exchanged, and the partners holding those interests are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of interest exchange and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(1)(b): the acquiring entity becomes the interest holder of the interests in the acquired partnership stated in the plan of interest exchange to be acquired by the acquiring entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(1)(c): the provisions of the partnership agreement of the acquired partnership that are to be in a record, if any, are amended to the extent provided in the plan of interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(2): Except as otherwise provided in the partnership agreement of a domestic acquired partnership, the interest exchange does not give rise to any rights that a partner or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the acquired partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(3): When an interest exchange becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to a domestic acquired partnership and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the interest exchange has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the interest exchange becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(4): (4)(a) When an interest exchange becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic acquired partnership with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(4)(a): The interest exchange does not discharge any interest holder liability to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the interest exchange became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(4)(b): The person does not have interest holder liability for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the interest exchange becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1036(4)(c): (4)(a) The person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the partnership agreement of the acquired entity with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1043 Approval of conversion.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1043(1): A plan of conversion is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1043(1)(a): by a domestic converting partnership by all the partners of the partnership entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1043(1)(b): in a record, by each partner of a domestic converting partnership that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the conversion becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1043(1)(b)(i): the partnership agreement provides in a record for the approval of a conversion or a merger in which some or all of its partners become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the interest holders; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1043(1)(b)(ii): the partner voted for or consented in a record to that provision of the partnership agreement or became a partner after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1043(2): A conversion involving a domestic converting entity that is not a partnership, including a subject entity, is not effective unless it is approved by the domestic converting entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1043(3): A conversion of a foreign converting entity is not effective unless it is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044 Amendment or abandonment of plan of conversion.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(1): A plan of conversion of a subject entity or domestic converting partnership may be amended:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(1)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(1)(b): by the partners of the entity in the manner provided in the plan, but a partner that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the conversion is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(1)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by any of the partners of the converting entity under the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(1)(b)(ii): the public organic record or private organic rules of the converted entity that will be in effect immediately after the conversion becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the interest holders of the converted entity under its organic law or organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(1)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the partner in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(2): After a plan of conversion has been approved and before a statement of conversion becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic converting partnership may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(3): If a plan of conversion is abandoned after a statement of conversion has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement of conversion becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by the converting entity, must be delivered to the division for filing before the time the statement of conversion becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the conversion is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(3)(a): the name of the converting subject entity or partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(3)(b): the date on which the statement of conversion was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1044(3)(c): a statement that the conversion has been abandoned in accordance with this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046 Effect of conversion.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1): 48-1d-1008 When a conversion in which the converted entity is a subject entity or domestic partnership becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(a): the converted entity is:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(a)(i): organized under and subject to this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(a)(ii): the same entity without interruption as the converting entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(b): all property of the converting entity continues to be vested in the converted entity without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(c): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the converting entity continue as debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the converted entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(d): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of conversion, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of the converting entity remain in the converted entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(e): the name of the converted entity may be substituted for the name of the converting entity in any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(f): if the converted entity is a limited liability partnership, its statement of qualification is effective simultaneously;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(g): the provisions of the partnership agreement of the converted entity that are to be in a record, if any, approved as part of the plan of conversion are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(1)(h): 48-1d-1008 the interests in the converting entity are converted, and the interest holders of the converting entity are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of conversion and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(2): Except as otherwise provided in the partnership agreement of a domestic converting partnership, the conversion does not give rise to any rights that a partner or third party would otherwise have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the converting entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(3): When a conversion becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to the converting entity and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the conversion has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the conversion becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(4): (4)(a) When a conversion becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic partnership with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(4)(a): The conversion does not discharge any interest holder liability to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the conversion became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(4)(b): The person does not have interest holder liability for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the conversion becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(4)(c): (4)(a) The person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the partnership agreement of the converting entity with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(5): 16-17-301 When a conversion becomes effective, a foreign entity that is the converted entity may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any of its debts, obligations, and other liabilities as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(6): If the converting entity is a registered foreign entity, its registration to do business in this state is canceled when the conversion becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1046(7): A conversion does not require the entity to wind up its affairs and does not constitute or cause the dissolution of the entity.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1053 Approval of domestication.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1053(1): A plan of domestication of a domestic domesticating limited liability partnership is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1053(1)(a): by all the partners entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1053(1)(b): in a record, by each partner that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the domestication becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1053(1)(b)(i): the partnership agreement of the entity provides in a record for the approval of a domestication or merger in which some or all of its partners become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the partners; and

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1053(2): A domestication of a foreign domesticating limited liability partnership is not effective unless it is approved in accordance with the law of the foreign limited liability partnership's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1054 Amendment or abandonment of plan of domestication.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1054(2): After a plan of domestication has been approved by a domestic domesticating limited liability partnership and before a statement of domestication becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic domesticating limited liability partnership may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056 Effect of domestication.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1): 48-1d-1008 When a domestication becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(a): the domesticated limited liability partnership is:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(a)(i): organized under and subject to the organic law of the domesticated limited liability partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(a)(ii): the same entity without interruption as the domesticating limited liability partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(b): all property of the domesticating limited liability partnership continues to be vested in the domesticated entity without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(c): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the domesticating limited liability partnership continue as debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the domesticated limited liability partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(d): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of domestication, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of the domesticating limited liability partnership remain in the domesticated limited liability partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(e): the name of the domesticated limited liability partnership may be substituted for the name of the domesticating limited liability partnership in any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(f): the statement of qualification of the domestic limited liability partnership is effective;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(g): the provisions of the partnership agreement of the domesticated limited liability partnership that are to be in a record, if any, approved as part of the plan of domestication are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(1)(h): 48-1d-1008 the interests in the domesticating limited liability partnership are converted to the extent and as approved in connection with the domestication, and the partners of the domesticating limited liability partnership are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of domestication and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(2): Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or partnership agreement of the domesticating limited liability partnership, the domestication does not give rise to any rights that a partner or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the domesticating limited liability partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(3): When a domestication becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to the domesticating limited liability partnership and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic limited liability partnership as a result of the domestication has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the domestic limited liability partnership and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(4): (4)(a) When a domestication becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(4)(a): The domestication does not discharge any interest holder liability under this part to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the domestication became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(4)(b): A person does not have interest holder liability under this chapter for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arise after the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(4)(c): (4)(a) A person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, or this chapter, or the partnership agreement of a domestic domesticating limited liability partnership with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(5): 16-17-301 When a domestication becomes effective, a foreign limited liability partnership that is the domesticated limited liability partnership may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any of its debts, obligations, and other liabilities as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(6): If the domesticating limited liability partnership is a registered foreign limited liability partnership, the registration of the foreign limited liability partnership is canceled when the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1056(7): A domestication does not require the limited liability partnership to wind up its business and does not constitute or cause the dissolution of the limited liability partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1101 Statement of qualification.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1101(1): A partnership may become a limited liability partnership pursuant to this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1101(2): The terms and conditions on which a partnership becomes a limited liability partnership must be approved by the vote or consent necessary to amend the partnership agreement except, in the case of a partnership agreement that expressly addresses obligations to contribute to the partnership, the vote or consent necessary to amend those provisions.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103 Reinstatement.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(1): 48-1d-1102; 48-1d-1105; 16-17-203 A limited liability partnership whose statement of qualification has been revoked administratively under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(1)(a): 48-1d-1105 the name of the partnership at the time of the administrative revocation of its statement of qualification and, if needed, a different name that satisfies Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(1)(b): 16-17-203 the address of the principal office of the partnership and information required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(1)(c): the effective date of administrative revocation of the partnership's statement of qualification; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(1)(d): that the grounds for revocation did not exist or have been cured.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(2): 48-1d-1102 A limited liability partnership whose statement of qualification has been revoked administratively under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(3): 42-2-6.6 A limited liability partnership retains the limited liability partnership's name and assumed name, as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(4): To have its statement of qualification reinstated, a partnership whose statement of qualification has been revoked administratively must pay all fees, taxes, and penalties that were due to the division at the time of the administrative revocation and all fees, taxes, and penalties that would have been due to the division while the partnership's statement of qualification was revoked administratively.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(5): If the division determines that the application contains the information required by Subsection (1) or (2), is satisfied that the information is correct, and determines that all payments required to be made to the division by Subsection (4) have been made, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(5)(a): cancel the statement of revocation and prepare a statement of reinstatement that states the division's determination and the effective date of reinstatement;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(5)(b): file the statement of revocation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(5)(c): serve a copy of the statement of revocation on the limited liability partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(6): When reinstatement under this section is effective, the following rules apply:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(6)(a): the reinstatement relates back to and takes effect as of the effective date of the administrative revocation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1103(6)(b): the partnership's status as a limited liability partnership continues as if the revocation had not occurred, except for the rights of a person arising out of an act or omission in reliance on the revocation before the person knew or had notice of the reinstatement are not affected.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1104 Judicial review of denial of reinstatement.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1104(1): If the division denies a limited liability partnership's application for reinstatement following administrative revocation of the limited liability partnership's statement of qualification, the division shall serve the limited liability company partnership with notice in a record that explains the reasons for the denial.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1104(2): A limited liability partnership may seek judicial review of denial of reinstatement in the district court not later than 30 days after service of the notice of denial.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1109(2): Information in an annual report must be current as of the date the report is signed by the limited liability partnership or registered foreign limited liability partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1109(3): A report must be delivered to the division for each year following the calendar year in which the limited liability partnership's statement of qualification became effective or the registered foreign limited liability partnership registered to do business in this state:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1109(3)(a): in the case of a limited liability partnership, the annual report must be delivered to the division during the month in which is the anniversary date on which the limited liability partnership statement of qualification became effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1109(3)(b): in the case of a registered foreign limited liability partnership, the annual report must be delivered to the division during the month in which is the anniversary date on which the registered foreign limited liability partnership registered to do business in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1109(4): If an annual report does not contain the information required by this section, the division promptly shall notify the reporting limited liability partnership or registered foreign limited liability partnership in a record and return the report for correction.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1109(5): 16-17-206 If an annual report contains the name or address of a registered agent which differs from the information shown in the records of the division immediately before the annual report becomes effective, the differing information in the annual report is considered a statement of change under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201 Governing law.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201(1): The law of the jurisdiction in which the statement of qualification or equivalent filing of a foreign limited liability partnership is filed governs:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201(1)(a): the internal affairs of the foreign limited liability partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201(1)(b): the liability of a partner as partner for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the foreign limited liability partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201(2): A foreign limited liability partnership is not precluded from registering to do business in this state because of any difference between the law of this state and the jurisdiction under which the foreign limited liability partnership's statement of qualification or equivalent filing is filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201(3): Registration of a foreign limited liability partnership to do business in this state does not authorize the foreign limited liability partnership to engage in any business or exercise any power that a domestic limited liability partnership may not engage in or exercise in this state as a limited liability partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201(4)(a): The division may permit a tribal limited liability partnership to apply for authority to transact business in the state in the same manner as a foreign limited liability partnership formed in another state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1201(4)(b): If a tribal limited liability partnership elects to apply for authority to transact business in the state, for purposes of this chapter, the tribal limited liability partnership shall be treated in the same manner as a foreign limited liability partnership formed under the laws of another state.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1202 Registration to do business in this state.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1202(1): A foreign limited liability partnership may not do business in this state until it registers with the division under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1202(2): A foreign limited liability partnership doing business in this state may not maintain an action or proceeding in this state unless it has registered to do business in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1202(3): The failure of a foreign limited liability partnership to register to do business in this state does not impair the validity of a contract or act of the foreign limited liability partnership or preclude it from defending an action or proceeding in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1202(4): A limitation on the liability of a partner of a foreign limited liability partnership is not waived solely because the foreign limited liability partnership does business in this state without registering to do business in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1202(5): 48-1d-1201(1); (2) Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1203(3): the jurisdiction in which the foreign limited liability partnership's statement of qualification or equivalent filing is filed;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1203(4): the street and mailing addresses of the foreign limited liability partnership's principal office and, if the law of the jurisdiction in which the foreign limited liability partnership's statement of qualification or equivalent filing is filed requires the foreign limited liability partnership to maintain an office in that jurisdiction, the street and mailing addresses of the required office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1203(5): 16-17-203(1) the information required by Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205 Activities not constituting doing business.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1): Activities of a foreign limited liability partnership which do not constitute doing business in this state under this part include:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(a): maintaining, defending, mediating, arbitrating, and settling an action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(b): carrying on any activity concerning its internal affairs, including meetings of its partners;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(c): maintaining accounts in financial institutions;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(d): maintaining offices or agencies for the transfer, exchange, and registration of securities of the foreign limited liability partnership or maintaining trustees or depositories with respect to those securities;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(e): selling through independent contractors;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(f): soliciting or obtaining orders by any means if the orders require acceptance outside this state before they become contracts;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(g): creating or acquiring indebtedness, mortgages, or security interests in property;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(h): securing or collecting debts or enforcing mortgages or security interests in property securing the debts, and holding, protecting, or maintaining property;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(i): conducting an isolated transaction that is not in the course of similar transactions;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(j): owning, without more, property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(1)(k): doing business in interstate commerce.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(2): A person does not do business in this state solely by being a partner of a foreign limited liability partnership that does business in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1205(3): This section does not apply in determining the contacts or activities that may subject a foreign limited liability partnership to service of process, taxation, or regulation under law of this state other than this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1207 Withdrawal deemed on conversion to domestic filing entity or domestic limited liability partnership.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A registered foreign limited liability partnership that converts to a domestic limited liability partnership or to a domestic entity that is organized, incorporated, or otherwise formed through the delivery of a record to the division for filing is deemed to have withdrawn its registration on the effective date of the conversion.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1211 Withdrawal of registration of registered foreign limited liability partnership.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1211(1): (2) A registered foreign limited liability partnership may withdraw its registration by delivering a statement of withdrawal to the division for filing.  The statement of withdrawal must state:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1211(1)(a): the name of the foreign limited liability partnership and the jurisdiction in which the foreign limited liability partnership's statement of qualification or equivalent filing is filed;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1211(1)(b): that the foreign limited liability partnership is not doing business in this state and that it withdraws its registration to do business in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1211(1)(c): that the foreign limited liability partnership revokes the authority of its registered agent to accept service on its behalf in this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1211(1)(d): (2) an address to which service of process may be made under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1211(2): 16-17-301(2) After the withdrawal of the registration of a foreign limited liability partnership, service of process in any action or proceeding based on a cause of action arising during the time the foreign limited liability partnership was registered to do business in this state may be made pursuant to Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1212 Action by attorney general.
------------------------------------------------------------
The attorney general may maintain an action to enjoin a foreign limited liability partnership from doing business in this state in violation of this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1301 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1301(1): "Professional services partnership" means a limited liability partnership organized in accordance with this part to provide professional services.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1301(2): "Regulating board" means the entity organized pursuant to state law that licenses and regulates the practice of the profession that a limited liability partnership is organized to provide.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1302 Application of this part.
----------------------------------------------------------
If a conflict arises between this part and another provision of this chapter, this part controls.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1303 Name limitations.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1303(1): 48-1d-1105; 48-1d-1206; 48-1d-1304 The name of a domestic professional services partnership and of a foreign professional services partnership authorized to transact business in this state, in addition to complying with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1303(1)(a): 48-1d-1304 may not contain language stating or implying that it is formed for a purpose other than that authorized by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1303(1)(b): must conform with any rule made by the regulating board having jurisdiction over a professional service to be rendered by the professional service partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1303(2): 48-1d-1105; 48-1d-1206 Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1303(2)(a): the personal name of an individual partner or individual former partner of the professional services partnership; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1303(2)(b): the name of an individual who was associated with a predecessor of the professional services partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1304 Providing a professional service.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1304(1): 48-1d-1305 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1304(2): (1) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1304(2)(a): require an individual employed by a professional services partnership to be licensed to perform a service for the professional services company if a license is not otherwise required;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1304(2)(b): prohibit a licensed individual from providing a professional service in the individual's professional capacity although the individual is a partner, employee, or agent of a professional services partnership; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1304(2)(c): prohibit an individual licensed in another state from providing a professional service for a professional services partnership in this state if not prohibited by the regulating board.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305 Limit of one profession.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(1): (1)(a) A professional services partnership organized to provide a professional service under this part may provide only:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(1)(a): one specific type of professional service; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(1)(b): (1)(a) services ancillary to the professional service described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(2): (2)(a) A professional services partnership organized to provide a professional service under this part may not engage in a business other than to provide:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(2)(a): the professional service that it was organized to provide; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(2)(b): (2)(a) services ancillary to the professional service described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(3): (1); (2) Notwithstanding Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(3)(a): own real and personal property necessary or appropriate for providing the type of professional service it was organized to provide; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(3)(b): invest the professional services partnership's money in one or more of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(3)(b)(i): real estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(3)(b)(ii): mortgages;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(3)(b)(iii): stocks;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(3)(b)(iv): bonds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1305(3)(b)(v): another type of investment.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1306 Activity limitations.
------------------------------------------------------
A professional services partnership may not do anything that an individual licensed to practice the profession that the professional services partnership is organized to provide is prohibited from doing.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1307 This part does not limit regulating board.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
This part does not restrict the authority or duty of a regulating board to license an individual providing a professional service or the practice of the profession that is within the jurisdiction of the regulating board, notwithstanding that the individual:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1307(1): is a partner or employee of a professional services partnership; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1307(2): provides the professional service or engages in the practice of the profession through a professional services partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1308 Partner of a professional services partnership.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A professional services partnership organized to provide a professional service:Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1308(1): may include a partner or employee who is authorized under the laws of the jurisdiction where the partner or employee resides to provide a similar professional service;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1308(2): may include a partner who is not licensed or registered by the state to provide the professional service to the extent allowed by the applicable licensing or registration act relating to the professional service; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1308(3): may render a professional service in this state only through a partner or employee who is licensed or registered by this state to render the professional service.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1401 Uniformity of application and construction.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this chapter, consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among states that enact the uniform act upon which this chapter is based.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1402 Severability clause.
-----------------------------------------------------
If any provision of this chapter or its application to any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect other provisions or applications of this chapter which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this chapter are severable.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1403 Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter modifies, limits, and supersedes the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001 et seq., but this chapter does not modify, limit, or supersede Sec. 101(c) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in Sec. 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7003(b).

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1404 Savings clause.
------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not affect an action commenced, proceeding brought, or right accrued before this chapter takes effect.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1405 Application to existing relationships.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1405(1): (3) Before January 1, 2016, this chapter governs only:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1405(1)(a): a partnership formed on or after January 1, 2014; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1405(1)(b): (3) except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1405(2): (3) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1405(3): (1)(b); (3)(a)(ii) With respect to a partnership that elects pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-1d-1405(3)(a): before January 1, 2016, to:
