Utah Code Annotated - Title 48 - Chapter 2e - Utah Uniform Limited Partnership Act
**********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah Uniform Limited Partnership Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(1): 48-2e-201 "Certificate of limited partnership" means the certificate required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(2): 48-2e-501 "Contribution," except in the phrase "right of contribution," means property or a benefit described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(3): "Debtor in bankruptcy" means a person that is the subject of:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(3)(a): an order for relief under Title 11 of the United States Code or a comparable order under a successor statute of general application; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(3)(b): a comparable order under federal, state, or foreign law governing insolvency.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(4): "Distribution" means a transfer of money or other property from a limited partnership to a person on account of a transferable interest or in the person's capacity as a partner.  The term:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(4)(a): includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(4)(a)(i): a redemption or other purchase by a limited partnership of a transferable interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(4)(a)(ii): a transfer to a partner in return for the partner's relinquishment of any right to participate as a partner in the management or conduct of the limited partnership's activities and affairs or to have access to records or other information concerning the limited partnership's activities and affairs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(4)(b): does not include amounts constituting reasonable compensation for present or past service or payments made in the ordinary course of business under a bona fide retirement plan or other bona fide benefits program.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(5): "Division" means the Division of Corporations and Commercial Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(6): 48-2e-404(3) "Foreign limited liability limited partnership" means a foreign limited partnership whose general partners have limited liability for the debts, obligations, or other liabilities of the foreign limited partnership under a provision similar to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(7): "Foreign limited partnership" means an unincorporated entity formed under the law of a jurisdiction other than this state which would be a limited partnership if formed under the law of this state.  The term includes a foreign limited liability limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(8): 48-2e-401; 48-2e-1205; 48-2e-603 "General partner" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(8)(a): 48-2e-401; 48-2e-1205 has become a general partner under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(8)(b): 48-2e-603 has not dissociated as a general partner under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(9): "Jurisdiction," used to refer to a political entity, means the United States, a state, a foreign country, or a political subdivision of a foreign country.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(10): "Jurisdiction of formation" means, with respect to an entity, the jurisdiction:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(10)(a): under whose law the entity is formed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(10)(b): in the case of a limited liability partnership or foreign limited liability partnership, in which the partnership's statement of qualification is filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(11): "Limited liability limited partnership," except in the phrase "foreign limited liability limited partnership," means a limited partnership whose certificate of limited partnership states that the partnership is a limited liability limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(12): 48-2e-301; 48-2e-1205; 48-2e-601 "Limited partner" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(12)(a): 48-2e-301; 48-2e-1205 has become a limited partner under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(12)(b): 48-2e-601 has not dissociated under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(13): Part 11, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; 48-2e-1205 "Limited partnership" means an entity formed under this chapter or which becomes subject to this chapter under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(14): "Partner" means a limited partner or general partner.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(15): 48-2e-112(1) "Partnership agreement" means the agreement, whether or not referred to as a partnership agreement, and whether oral, implied, in a record, or in any combination thereof, of all the partners of a limited partnership concerning the matters described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(16): "Person" means an individual, business corporation, nonprofit corporation, partnership, limited partnership, limited liability company, limited cooperative association, unincorporated nonprofit association, statutory trust, business trust, common-law business trust, estate, trust, association, joint venture, public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality, or any other legal or commercial entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(17): "Principal office" means the principal executive office of a limited partnership or foreign limited partnership, whether or not the office is located in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(18): "Property" means all property, whether real, personal, or mixed or tangible or intangible, or any right or interest therein.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(19): "Record," used as a noun, means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(20): "Registered agent" means an agent of a limited partnership or foreign limited partnership which is authorized to receive service of any process, notice, or demand required or permitted by law to be served on the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(21): "Registered foreign limited partnership" means a foreign limited partnership that is registered to do business in this state pursuant to a statement of registration filed by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(22): 48-2e-115 "Required information" means the information that a limited partnership is required to maintain under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(23): "Sign" means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a record:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(23)(a): to execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(23)(b): to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic symbol, sound, or process.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(24): "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(25): "Transfer" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(25)(a): an assignment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(25)(b): a conveyance;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(25)(c): a sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(25)(d): a lease;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(25)(e): an encumbrance, including a mortgage or security interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(25)(f): a gift; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(25)(g): a transfer by operation of law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(26): "Transferable interest" means the right, as initially owned by a person in the person's capacity as a partner, to receive distributions from a limited partnership in accordance with the partnership agreement, whether or not the person remains a partner or continues to own any part of the right.  The term applies to any fraction of the interest, by whomever owned.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(27): 48-2e-602(1)(c); 48-2e-605(1)(d) "Transferee" means a person to which all or part of a transferable interest has been transferred, whether or not the transferor is a partner.  The term includes a person that owns a transferable interest under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(28): "Tribal limited partnership" means a limited partnership:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(28)(a): formed under the law of a tribe; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(28)(b): that is at least 51% owned or controlled by the tribe under whose law the limited partnership is formed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-102(29): "Tribe" means a tribe, band, nation, pueblo, or other organized group or community of Indians, including an Alaska Native village, that is legally recognized as eligible for and is consistent with a special program, service, or entitlement provided by the United States to Indians because of their status as Indians.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-103 Knowledge -- Notice.
----------------------------------------------------

A limited partner's knowledge or notice of a fact relating to the limited partnership is not effective as knowledge of or notice to the limited partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-104 Nature, purpose, and duration of limited partnership.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-104(1): A limited partnership is an entity distinct from its partners.  A limited partnership is the same entity regardless of whether its certificate states that the limited partnership is a limited liability limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-104(2): A limited partnership may have any lawful purpose, regardless of whether for profit.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-104(3): A limited partnership has perpetual duration.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-105 Powers.
---------------------------------------
A limited partnership has the capacity to sue and be sued in its own name and the power to do all things necessary or convenient to carry on its activities and affairs.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-106 Governing law.
----------------------------------------------
The law of this state governs:Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-106(1): the internal affairs of a limited partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-106(2): the liability of a partner as partner for the debts, obligations, or other liabilities of a limited partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-107 Supplemental principles of law.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Unless displaced by particular provisions of this chapter, the principles of law and equity supplement this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-108 Permitted names.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-108(1): The name of a limited partnership may contain the name of any partner.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-108(2): The name of a limited partnership that is not a limited liability limited partnership shall contain the words "limited partnership" or the abbreviation "L.P." or "LP" and may not contain the words "limited liability limited partnership" or the abbreviation "L.L.L.P." or "LLLP".
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-108(3): The name of a limited liability limited partnership shall contain the words "limited liability limited partnership" or the abbreviation "LLLP" or "L.L.L.P." and may not contain the abbreviation "L.P." or "LP".

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-110 Registration of name.
-----------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-113 Partnership agreement -- Effect on limited partnership and person becoming partner -- Preformation agreement.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-113(1): A limited partnership is bound by and may enforce the partnership agreement, whether or not the limited partnership has itself manifested assent to the partnership agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-113(2): A person that becomes a partner of a limited partnership is deemed to assent to the partnership agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-113(3): Two or more persons intending to become the initial partners of a limited partnership may make an agreement providing that upon the formation of the limited partnership the agreement will become the limited partnership agreement.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114 Partnership agreement -- Effect on third parties and relationship to records effective on behalf of limited partnership.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114(1): A partnership agreement may specify that its amendment requires the approval of a person that is not a party to the partnership agreement or the satisfaction of a condition.  An amendment is ineffective if its adoption does not include the required approval or satisfy the specified condition.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114(2): 48-2e-703(2)(b) The obligations of a limited partnership and its partners to a person in the person's capacity as a transferee or person dissociated as a partner are governed by the partnership agreement.  Subject only to a court order issued under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114(2)(a): is effective with regard to any debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited partnership or its partners to the person in the person's capacity as a transferee or person dissociated as a partner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114(2)(b): is not effective to the extent the amendment imposes a new debt, obligation, or other liability on the transferee or person dissociated as a partner.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114(3): 48-2e-112(3); (4)(b) If a record delivered by a limited partnership to the division for filing becomes effective and contains a provision that would be ineffective under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114(4): (3) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114(4)(a): the partnership agreement prevails as to partners, persons dissociated as partners, and transferees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-114(4)(b): the record prevails as to other persons to the extent they reasonably rely on the record.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115 Required information.
-----------------------------------------------------
A limited partnership shall maintain at its principal office the following information:Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(1): a current list showing the full name and last known street and mailing address of each partner, separately identifying the general partners, in alphabetical order, and the limited partners, in alphabetical order;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(2): a copy of the initial certificate of limited partnership and all amendments to and restatements of the certificate, together with signed copies of any powers of attorney under which any certificate, amendment, or restatement has been signed;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(3): a copy of any filed statement of merger, interest exchange, conversion, or domestication;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(4): a copy of the limited partnership's federal, state, and local income tax returns and reports, if any, for the three most recent years;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(5): a copy of any partnership agreement made in a record and any amendment made in a record to any partnership agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(6): a copy of any financial statement of the limited partnership for the three most recent years;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(7): 48-2e-212 a copy of the three most recent annual reports delivered by the limited partnership to the division pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(8): a copy of any record made by the limited partnership during the past three years of any consent given by or vote taken of any partner pursuant to this chapter or the partnership agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(9): unless contained in a partnership agreement made in a record, a record stating:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(9)(a): a description and statement of the agreed value of contributions other than money made and agreed to be made by each partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(9)(b): the times at which, or events on the happening of which, any additional contributions agreed to be made by each partner are to be made;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(9)(c): for any person that is both a general partner and a limited partner, a specification of what transferable interest the person owns in each capacity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-115(9)(d): any events upon the happening of which the limited partnership is to be dissolved and its activities and affairs wound up.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-116 Dual capacity.
----------------------------------------------
A person may be both a general partner and a limited partner.  A person that is both a general and limited partner has the rights, powers, duties, and obligations provided by this chapter and the partnership agreement in each of those capacities.  When the person acts as a general partner, the person is subject to the obligations, duties, and restrictions under this chapter and the partnership agreement for general partners.  When the person acts as a limited partner, the person is subject to the obligations, duties, and restrictions under this chapter and the partnership agreement for limited partners.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-117 Delivery of record.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-117(1): Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, permissible means of delivery of a record include delivery by hand, the United States Postal Service, a commercial delivery service, and electronic transmission.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-117(2): Delivery to the division is effective only when a record is received by the division.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-118 Reservation of power to amend or repeal.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Legislature of this state has power to amend or repeal all or part of this chapter at any time, and all domestic and foreign limited partnerships subject to this chapter are governed by the amendment or repeal.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-201 Formation of limited partnership -- Certificate of limited partnership.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205 Filing requirements.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(1): To be filed by the division pursuant to this chapter, a record must be received by the division, comply with this chapter, and satisfy the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(1)(a): The filing of the record must be required or permitted by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(1)(b): The record must be physically delivered in written form unless and to the extent the division permits electronic delivery of records.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(1)(c): The record must be typewritten or computer generated.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(1)(d): The words in the record must be in English, and numbers must be in Arabic or Roman numerals, but the name of an entity need not be in English if written in English letters or Arabic or Roman numerals.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(1)(e): The record must be signed by a person authorized under this chapter to sign the record.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(1)(f): The record must state the name and capacity, if any, of each individual who signed it, either on behalf of the individual or the person authorized or required to sign the record, but need not contain a seal, attestation, acknowledgment, or verification.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(2): If law other than this chapter prohibits the disclosure by the division of information contained in a record delivered to the division for filing, the division shall accept the record if the record otherwise complies with this chapter but the division may redact the information.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(3): When a record is delivered to the division for filing, any fee required under this chapter and any fee, tax, interest, or penalty required to be paid under this chapter, or law other than this chapter, must be paid in a manner permitted by the division or by that law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-205(4): The division may require that a record delivered in written form be accompanied by an identical or conformed copy.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-206 Effective time and date.
--------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in SectionUtah Code Annotated § 48-2e-206(1): 48-2e-209 on the date and at the time of its filing by the division, as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-206(2): (1) on the date of filing and at the time specified in the record as its effective time, if later than the time under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-206(3): at a specified delayed effective time and date, which may not be more than 90 days after the date of filing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-206(4): if a delayed effective date is specified, but no time is specified, at 12:01 a.m. on the date specified, which may not be more than 90 days after the date of filing.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-207 Withdrawal of filed record before effectiveness.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-207(1): 48-2e-1124; 48-2e-1134; 48-2e-1144; 48-2e-1154 Except as otherwise provided in Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-207(2)(b): identify the record to be withdrawn; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-207(2)(c): if signed by fewer than all the persons that signed the record being withdrawn, state that the record is withdrawn in accordance with the agreement of all the persons that signed the record.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-207(3): On filing by the division of a statement of withdrawal, the action or transaction evidenced by the original record does not take effect.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208 Correcting filed record.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(1): A person on whose behalf a filed record was delivered to the division for filing may correct the record if:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(1)(a): the record at the time of filing was inaccurate;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(1)(b): the record was defectively signed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(1)(c): the electronic transmission of the record to the division was defective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(2): To correct a filed record, a person on whose behalf the record was delivered to the division must deliver to the division for filing a statement of correction.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(3): A statement of correction:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(3)(a): may not state a delayed effective date;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(3)(b): must be signed by the person correcting the filed record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(3)(c): must identify the filed record to be corrected;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(3)(d): must specify the inaccuracy or defect to be corrected; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(3)(e): must correct the inaccuracy or defect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-208(4): 48-2e-103(4) A statement of correction is effective as of the effective date of the filed record that it corrects except for purposes of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209 Duty of division to file -- Review of refusal to file -- Transmission of information by the division.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(1): The division shall file a record delivered to the division for filing which satisfies this chapter.  The duty of the division under this section is ministerial.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(2): When the division files a record, the division shall record it as filed on the date and at the time of its delivery.  After filing a record, the division shall deliver to the person that submitted the record a copy of the record with an acknowledgment of the date and time of filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(3): If the division refuses to file a record, the division, not later than 15 business days after the record is delivered, shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(3)(a): return the record or notify the person that submitted the record of the refusal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(3)(b): provide a brief explanation in a record of the reason for the refusal.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(4): Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(4)(a): Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration If the division refuses to file a record, the person that submitted the record may petition a court with jurisdiction under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(4)(b): The record and the explanation of the division of the refusal to file must be attached to the petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-209(4)(c): The court may decide the matter in a summary proceeding.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-301 Becoming limited partners.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-301(1): Upon formation of a limited partnership, a person becomes a limited partner as agreed among the persons that are to be the initial partners.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-301(2): Part 11, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; 48-2e-801(1)(d); (1)(e) After formation, a person becomes a limited partner:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-301(2)(c): with the affirmative vote or consent of all the partners; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-301(2)(d): 48-2e-801(1)(d); (1)(e) as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-301(3): A person may become a partner without:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-301(3)(a): acquiring a transferable interest; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-301(3)(b): making or being obligated to make a contribution to the limited partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-302 No agency power of limited partner as limited partner.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-302(1): A limited partner is not an agent of a limited partnership solely by reason of being a limited partner.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-302(2): A person's status as a limited partner does not prevent or restrict law other than this chapter from imposing liability on a limited partnership because of the person's conduct.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-303 No liability as limited partner for limited partnership obligations.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-303(1): A debt, obligation, or other liability of a limited partnership is not the debt, obligation, or other liability of a limited partner.  A limited partner is not personally liable, directly or indirectly, by way of contribution or otherwise, for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited partnership solely by reason of being or acting as a limited partner, even if the limited partner participates in the management and control of the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-303(2): The failure of a limited partnership to observe formalities relating to the exercise of its powers or management of its activities and affairs is not a ground for imposing liability on a limited partner for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited partnership.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The limited partner need not have any particular purpose for seeking the information.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-401 Becoming general partner.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-401(2)(b): making or being obligated to make a contribution to the limited partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-402 General partner agent of limited partnership.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-402(1): Each general partner is an agent of the limited partnership for the purposes of its activities and affairs.  An act of a general partner, including the signing of a record in the limited partnership's name, for apparently carrying on in the ordinary course the limited partnership's activities and affairs or activities and affairs of the kind carried on by the limited partnership binds the limited partnership, unless the general partner did not have authority to act for the limited partnership in the particular matter and the person with which the general partner was dealing knew or had notice that the general partner lacked authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-402(2): An act of a general partner which is not apparently for carrying on in the ordinary course the limited partnership's activities and affairs or activities and affairs of the kind carried on by the limited partnership binds the limited partnership only if the act was actually authorized by all the other partners.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-403 Limited partnership liable for general partner's actionable conduct.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-403(1): A limited partnership is liable for loss or injury caused to a person, or for a penalty incurred, as a result of a wrongful act or omission, or other actionable conduct, of a general partner acting in the ordinary course of activities and affairs of the limited partnership or with the actual or apparent authority of the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-403(2): If, in the course of a limited partnership's activities and affairs or while acting with actual or apparent authority of the limited partnership, a general partner receives or causes the limited partnership to receive money or property of a person not a partner, and the money or property is misapplied by a general partner, the limited partnership is liable for the loss.

------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-404(1): (2); (3) Except as otherwise provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-404(2): A person that becomes a general partner of an existing limited partnership is not personally liable for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited partnership incurred before the person became a general partner.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-404(3): (3); 48-2e-406(2)(b) A debt, obligation, or other liability of a limited partnership incurred while the limited partnership is a limited liability limited partnership is solely the debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited liability limited partnership.  A general partner is not personally liable, directly or indirectly, by way of contribution or otherwise, for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited liability limited partnership solely by reason of being or acting as a general partner.  This Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-404(4): The failure of a limited liability limited partnership to observe formalities relating to the exercise of its powers or management of its activities and affairs is not a ground for imposing liability on a general partner of the limited liability limited partnership for a debt, obligation, or liability of the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-404(5): An amendment of a certificate of limited partnership which deletes a statement that the limited partnership is a limited liability limited partnership does not affect the limitation in this section on liability of a general partner for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the limited partnership incurred before the amendment became effective.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-406 Management rights of general partner.
---------------------------------------------------------------------

Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, any matter relating to the activities and affairs of the limited partnership is decided exclusively by the general partner or, if there is more than one general partner, by a majority of the general partners.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409 Standards of conduct for general partners.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(1): 48-2e-1001(1); (2); (3) A general partner owes to the limited partnership and, subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(2): The duty of loyalty of a general partner includes the duties:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(2)(a): to account to the limited partnership and hold as trustee for it any property, profit, or benefit derived by the general partner:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(2)(a)(i): in the conduct or winding up of the limited partnership's activities and affairs;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(2)(a)(ii): from a use by the general partner of the limited partnership's property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(2)(a)(iii): from the appropriation of a limited partnership opportunity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(2)(b): to refrain from dealing with the limited partnership in the conduct or winding up of the limited partnership's activities and affairs as or on behalf of a person having an interest adverse to the limited partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(2)(c): to refrain from competing with the limited partnership in the conduct or winding up of the limited partnership's activities and affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(3): The duty of care of a general partner in the conduct or winding up of the limited partnership's activities and affairs is to refrain from engaging in grossly negligent or reckless conduct, intentional misconduct, or a knowing violation of law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(4): A general partner shall discharge the duties and obligations under this chapter or under the partnership agreement and exercise any rights consistently with the contractual obligation of good faith and fair dealing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(5): A general partner does not violate a duty or obligation under this chapter or under the partnership agreement solely because the general partner's conduct furthers the general partner's own interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-409(6): All the partners of a limited partnership may authorize or ratify, after full disclosure of all material facts, a specific act or transaction by a general partner that otherwise would violate the duty of loyalty.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-501 Form of contribution.
-----------------------------------------------------
A contribution may consist of property transferred to, services performed for, or another benefit provided to the limited partnership or an agreement to transfer property to, perform services for, or provide another benefit to the limited partnership.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-502 Liability for contribution.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-502(1): A person's obligation to make a contribution to a limited partnership is not excused by the person's death, disability, dissolution, or other inability to perform personally.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-502(2): If a person does not fulfill an obligation to make a contribution other than money, the person is obligated at the option of the limited partnership to contribute money equal to the value, as stated in the required information, of the part of the contribution which has not been made.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-502(3): (1) The obligation of a person to make a contribution may be compromised only by the affirmative vote or consent of all partners.  If a creditor of a limited partnership extends credit or otherwise acts in reliance on an obligation described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-503(3): 48-2e-813(5) A person does not have a right to demand or receive a distribution from a limited partnership in any form other than money.  Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-503(4): If a partner or transferee becomes entitled to receive a distribution, the partner or transferee has the status of, and is entitled to all remedies available to, a creditor of the limited partnership with respect to the distribution.  However, the limited partnership's obligation to make a distribution is subject to offset for any amount owed to the limited partnership by the partner or a person dissociated as a partner on whose account the distribution is made.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-601 Dissociation as limited partner.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-601(1): A person does not have a right to dissociate as a limited partner before the completion of the winding up of the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-601(2): 48-2e-703; 48-2e-305(1); Part 11, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; Part 11, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; Part 11, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; Part 11, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication A person is dissociated as a limited partner when:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-601(2)(d)(ii): 48-2e-703 there has been a transfer of all of the person's transferable interest in the limited partnership, other than:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-601(2)(d)(iii)(B): not later than 90 days after the notification the statement of dissolution or the equivalent has not been revoked or its charter or right to conduct business has not been reinstated; or

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-601(2)(g): in the case of a person that is a testamentary or inter vivos trust or is acting as a limited partner by virtue of being a trustee of such a trust, the trust's entire transferable interest in the limited partnership is distributed;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-601(2)(h): in the case of a person that is an estate or is acting as a limited partner by virtue of being a personal representative of an estate, the estate's entire transferable interest in the limited partnership is distributed;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-601(2)(i): in the case of a person that is not an individual, corporation, unincorporated entity, trust, or estate, the existence of the person terminates;

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-701 Nature of transferable interest.
----------------------------------------------------------------
The only interest of a partner which is transferable is the partner's transferable interest.  A transferable interest is personal property.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702 Transfer of transferable interest.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(1): 48-2e-704; (3) A transfer, in whole or in part, of a transferable interest:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(1)(b): does not by itself cause the person's dissociation or a dissolution and winding up of the limited partnership's activities and affairs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(1)(c): 48-2e-704; (3) subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(1)(c)(i): participate in the management or conduct of the limited partnership's activities or affairs; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(1)(c)(ii): (3) except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(2): A transferee has the right to receive, in accordance with the transfer, distributions to which the transferor would otherwise be entitled.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(3): In a dissolution and winding up of a limited partnership, a transferee is entitled to an account of the limited partnership's transactions only from the date of dissolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(4): A transferable interest may be evidenced by a certificate of the interest issued by a limited partnership in a record, and, subject to this section, the interest represented by the certificate may be transferred by a transfer of the certificate.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(5): A limited partnership need not give effect to a transferee's rights under this section until the limited partnership knows or has notice of the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-702(6): A transfer of a transferable interest in violation of a restriction on transfer contained in the partnership agreement is ineffective as to a person having knowledge or notice of the restriction at the time of transfer.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703 Charging order.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(1): On application by a judgment creditor of a partner or transferee, a court may enter a charging order against the transferable interest of the judgment debtor for the unsatisfied amount of the judgment.  A charging order constitutes a lien on a judgment debtor's transferable interest and, after the limited partnership has been served with the charging order, requires the limited partnership to pay over to the person to which the charging order was issued any distribution that otherwise would be paid to the judgment debtor.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(2): (1) To the extent necessary to effectuate the collection of distributions pursuant to a charging order in effect under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(2)(a): appoint a receiver of the distributions subject to the charging order, with the power to make all inquiries the judgment debtor might have made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(2)(b): make all other orders necessary to give effect to the charging order.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(3): 48-2e-702 Upon a showing that distributions under a charging order will not pay the judgment debt within a reasonable time, the court may foreclose the lien and order the sale of the transferable interest.  The purchaser at the foreclosure sale obtains only the transferable interest, does not thereby become a partner, and is subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(4): (3); (1) At any time before foreclosure under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(5): (3) At any time before foreclosure under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(6): This chapter does not deprive any partner or transferee of the benefit of any exemption law applicable to the transferable interest of the partner or transferee.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-703(7): This section provides the exclusive remedy by which a person seeking to enforce a judgment against a partner or transferee may, in the capacity of judgment creditor, satisfy the judgment from the judgment debtor's transferable interest.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801 Events causing dissolution.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1): 48-2e-810 A limited partnership is dissolved, and the limited partnership's activities and affairs must be wound up, upon the occurrence of any of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(a): an event or circumstance that the partnership agreement states causes dissolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(b): the affirmative vote or consent of all general partners and of limited partners owning a majority of the rights to receive distributions as limited partners at the time the vote or consent is to be effective;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(c): after the dissociation of a person as a general partner:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(c)(i): if the limited partnership has at least one remaining general partner, the vote or consent to dissolve the limited partnership not later than 90 days after the dissociation by partners owning a majority of the rights to receive distributions as partners at the time the vote or consent is to be effective; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(c)(ii): if the limited partnership does not have a remaining general partner, the passage of 90 days after the dissociation, unless before the end of the period:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(c)(ii)(A): consent to continue the activities and affairs of the limited partnership and admit at least one general partner is given by limited partners owning a majority of the rights to receive distributions as limited partners at the time the consent is to be effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(c)(ii)(B): at least one person is admitted as a general partner in accordance with the consent;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(d): the passage of 90 consecutive days after the dissociation of the limited partnership's last limited partner, unless before the end of the period the limited partnership admits at least one limited partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(e): the passage of 90 consecutive days during which the limited partnership has only one partner, unless before the end of the period:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(e)(i): the limited partnership admits at least one person as a partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(e)(ii): if the previously sole remaining partner is only a general partner, the limited partnership admits the person as a limited partner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(e)(iii): if the previously sole remaining partner is only a limited partner, the limited partnership admits a person as a general partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(f): upon a petition brought by a partner, the entry of a court order dissolving the limited partnership on the grounds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(f)(i): the conduct of all or substantially all the limited partnership's activities and affairs is unlawful; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(f)(ii): it is not reasonably practicable to carry on the limited partnership's activities and affairs in conformity with the partnership agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(1)(g): 48-2e-810 the signing and filing of a statement of administrative dissolution by the division under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(2): (1); (1) If an event occurs that imposes a deadline on a limited partnership under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(2)(a): the occurrence of the second event does not affect the deadline caused by the first event; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-801(2)(b): the limited partnership's meeting of the requirements of the first deadline does not extend the second deadline.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802 Winding up.
-------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(1): 48-2e-803
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(1)(a): A dissolved limited partnership shall wind up the limited partnership's activities and affairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(1)(b): 48-2e-803 Except as otherwise provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2): In winding up the limited partnership's activities and affairs, the limited partnership:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(a): shall discharge the limited partnership's debts, obligations, and other liabilities, settle and close the limited partnership's activities and affairs, and marshal and distribute the assets of the limited partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(b): may:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(b)(i): amend its certificate of limited partnership to state that the limited partnership is dissolved;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(b)(ii): preserve the limited partnership activities, affairs, and property as a going concern for a reasonable time;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(b)(iii): prosecute and defend actions and proceedings, whether civil, criminal, or administrative;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(b)(iv): transfer the limited partnership's property;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(b)(v): settle disputes by mediation or arbitration;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(b)(vi): deliver to the division for filing a statement of termination stating the name of the limited partnership and that the limited partnership is terminated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(2)(b)(vii): perform other acts necessary or appropriate to the winding up.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(3): (3); 48-2e-804
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(3)(a): If a dissolved limited partnership does not have a general partner, a person to wind up the dissolved limited partnership's activities and affairs may be appointed by the affirmative vote or consent of limited partners owning a majority of the rights to receive distributions as limited partners at the time the vote or consent is to be effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(3)(b): (3); 48-2e-804 A person appointed under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(3)(b)(i): 48-2e-804 has the powers of a general partner under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(3)(b)(ii)(C): that the person has been appointed pursuant to this subsection to wind up the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-802(4): (3) Upon a petition brought by a partner, a court may order judicial supervision of the winding up of a dissolved limited partnership, including the appointment of a person to wind up the limited partnership's activities and affairs, if:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-811(5): If the division determines that an application under Subsection (1) or (2) contains the information required, is satisfied that the information is correct, and determines that all payments required to be made to the division by Subsection (4) have been made, the division shall:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-812 Judicial review of denial of reinstatement.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-812(1): If the division denies a limited partnership's application for reinstatement following administrative dissolution, the division shall serve the limited partnership with notice in a record that explains the reasons for the denial.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-812(2): A limited partnership may seek judicial review of denial of reinstatement in the district court not later than 30 days after service of the notice of denial.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901 Governing law.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901(1): The law of the jurisdiction of formation of a foreign limited partnership governs:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901(1)(a): the internal affairs of the foreign limited partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901(1)(b): the liability of a partner as partner for a debt, obligation, or other liability of the foreign limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901(2): A foreign limited partnership is not precluded from registering to do business in this state because of any difference between the law of its jurisdiction of formation and the law of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901(3): Registration of a foreign limited partnership to do business in this state does not authorize the foreign limited partnership to engage in any activities and affairs or exercise any power that a limited partnership may not engage in or exercise in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901(4)(a): The division may permit a tribal limited partnership to apply for authority to transact business in the state in the same manner as a foreign limited partnership formed in another state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-901(4)(b): If a tribal limited partnership elects to apply for authority to transact business in the state, for purposes of this chapter, the tribal limited partnership shall be treated in the same manner as a foreign limited partnership formed under the laws of another state.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-902 Registration to do business in this state.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-902(1): A foreign limited partnership may not do business in this state until it registers with the division under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-902(2): A foreign limited partnership doing business in this state may not maintain an action or proceeding in this state unless it is registered to do business in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-902(3): The failure of a foreign limited partnership to register to do business in this state does not impair the validity of a contract or act of the foreign limited partnership or preclude it from defending an action or proceeding in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-902(4): A limitation on the liability of a general partner or limited partners of a foreign limited partnership is not waived solely because the foreign limited partnership does business in this state without registering to do business in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-902(5): 48-2e-901(1); (2) Subsections

---------------------------------------------------------------
To register to do business in this state, a foreign limited partnership must deliver a foreign registration statement to the division for filing.  The statement must state:Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-903(1): 48-2e-108; 48-2e-906(1) the name of the foreign limited partnership and, if the name does not comply with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-903(2): that the limited partnership is a foreign limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-903(3): the name of the foreign limited partnership's jurisdiction of formation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-903(4): the street and mailing addresses of the foreign limited partnership's principal office and, if the law of the foreign limited partnership's jurisdiction of formation requires the foreign limited partnership to maintain an office in that jurisdiction, the street and mailing addresses of the required office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-903(5): 16-17-203(1) the information required by Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905 Activities not constituting doing business.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1): Activities of a foreign limited partnership which do not constitute doing business in this state under this part include:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(a): maintaining, defending, mediating, arbitrating, and settling an action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(b): carrying on any activity concerning its internal affairs, including holding meetings of its partners;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(c): maintaining accounts in financial institutions;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(d): maintaining offices or agencies for the transfer, exchange, and registration of securities of the foreign limited partnership or maintaining trustees or depositories with respect to those securities;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(e): selling through independent contractors;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(f): soliciting or obtaining orders by any means, if the orders require acceptance outside this state before they become contracts;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(g): creating or acquiring indebtedness, mortgages, or security interests in property;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(h): securing or collecting debts or enforcing mortgages or security interests in property securing the debts, and holding, protecting, or maintaining property;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(i): conducting an isolated transaction that is not in the course of similar transactions;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(j): owning, without more, property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(1)(k): doing business in interstate commerce.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-905(2): A person does not do business in this state solely by being a partner of a foreign limited partnership that does business in this state.  This section does not apply in determining the contacts or activities that may subject a foreign limited partnership to service of process, taxation, or regulation under law of this state other than this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-907 Withdrawal deemed on conversion to domestic filing entity or domestic limited liability partnership.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A registered foreign limited partnership that converts to a domestic limited liability partnership or to a domestic entity that is organized, incorporated, or otherwise formed through the delivery of a record to the division for filing is deemed to have withdrawn its registration on the effective date of the conversion.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908 Withdrawal on dissolution or conversion to nonfiling entity other than limited liability partnership.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1): (2) A registered foreign limited partnership that has dissolved and completed winding up or has converted to a domestic or foreign entity that is not organized, incorporated, or otherwise formed through the public filing of a record, other than a limited liability partnership, shall deliver a statement of withdrawal to the division for filing.  The statement must state:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1)(a): in the case of a foreign limited partnership that has completed winding up:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1)(a)(i): its name and jurisdiction of formation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1)(a)(ii): that the foreign limited partnership surrenders its registration to do business in this state as a registered foreign limited partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1)(b): (2) in the case of a foreign limited partnership that has converted:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1)(b)(i): the name of the converting foreign limited partnership and its jurisdiction of formation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1)(b)(ii): the type of entity to which the foreign limited partnership has converted and its jurisdiction of formation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1)(b)(iii): that the converted entity surrenders the converting partnership's registration to do business in this state and revokes the authority of the converting foreign limited partnership's registered agent to act as registered agent in this state on the behalf of the foreign limited partnership or the converted entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-908(1)(b)(iv): (2) a mailing address to which service of process may be made under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-909 Transfer of registration.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-909(1): 48-2e-108; 48-2e-906(1); 16-17-203(1) When a registered foreign limited partnership has merged into a foreign entity that is not registered to do business in this state or has converted to a foreign entity required to register with the division to do business in this state, the foreign entity shall deliver to the division for filing an application for transfer of registration.  The application must state:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-909(1)(a): the name of the registered foreign limited partnership before the merger or conversion;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-909(1)(b): that before the merger or conversion the registration pertained to a foreign limited partnership;

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-909(1)(e): the street and mailing addresses of the principal office of the applicant foreign entity and, if the law of the entity's jurisdiction of formation requires the entity to maintain an office in that jurisdiction, the street and mailing addresses of that office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-909(1)(f): 16-17-203(1) the information required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-909(2): When an application for transfer of registration takes effect, the registration of the foreign limited partnership to do business in this state is transferred without interruption to the foreign entity into which the foreign limited partnership has merged or to which it has been converted.
