Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-912 Action by attorney general.
-----------------------------------------------------------
The attorney general may maintain an action to enjoin a foreign limited partnership from doing business in this state in violation of this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1001 Direct action by partner.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1001(1): (2) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1001(2): A partner maintaining a direct action under this section must plead and prove an actual or threatened injury that is not solely the result of an injury suffered or threatened to be suffered by the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1001(3): A right to an accounting upon a dissolution and winding up does not revive a claim barred by law.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1002 Derivative action.
---------------------------------------------------
A partner may maintain a derivative action to enforce a right of a limited partnership if:Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1002(1): the partner first makes a demand on the general partners, requesting that they cause the limited partnership to bring an action to enforce the right, and the general partners do not bring the action within a reasonable time; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1002(2): (1) a demand under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1003 Proper plaintiff.
--------------------------------------------------
A derivative action to enforce a right of a limited partnership may be maintained only by a person that is a partner at the time the action is commenced and:Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1003(1): which was a partner when the conduct giving rise to the action occurred; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1003(2): whose status as a partner devolved on the person by operation of law or pursuant to the terms of the partnership agreement from a person that was a partner at the time of the conduct.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1004 Pleading.
------------------------------------------
In a derivative action to enforce a right of a limited partnership, the complaint must state with particularity:Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1004(1): the date and content of the plaintiff's demand and the response to the demand by the general partner; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1004(2): why demand should be excused as futile.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005 Special litigation committee.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(1): 48-2e-304; 48-2e-407 If a limited partnership is named as or made a party in a derivative proceeding, the limited partnership may appoint a special litigation committee to investigate the claims asserted in the proceeding and determine whether pursuing the action is in the best interests of the limited partnership.  If the limited partnership appoints a special litigation committee, on motion by the committee made in the name of the limited partnership, except for good cause shown, the court shall stay discovery for the time reasonably necessary to permit the committee to make its investigation.  This subsection does not prevent the court from:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(1)(a): 48-2e-304; 48-2e-407 enforcing a person's right to information under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(1)(b): granting extraordinary relief in the form of a temporary restraining order or preliminary injunction.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(2): A special litigation committee must be composed of one or more disinterested and independent individuals, who may be partners.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(3): A special litigation committee may be appointed:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(3)(a): by a majority of the general partners not named as parties in the proceeding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(3)(b): if all general partners are named as parties in the proceeding, by a majority of the general partners named as defendants.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(4): After appropriate investigation, a special litigation committee may determine that it is in the best interests of the limited partnership that the proceeding:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(4)(a): continue under the control of the plaintiff;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(4)(b): continue under the control of the committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(4)(c): be settled on terms approved by the committee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(4)(d): be dismissed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1005(5): (4); (1) After making a determination under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1006 Proceeds and expenses.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1006(1): (2) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1006(1)(a): any proceeds or other benefits of a derivative action, whether by judgment, compromise, or settlement, belong to the limited partnership and not to the plaintiff; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1006(1)(b): if the plaintiff receives any proceeds, the plaintiff shall remit them immediately to the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1006(2): If a derivative action is successful in whole or in part, the court may award the plaintiff reasonable expenses, including reasonable attorney's fees and costs, from the recovery of the limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1006(3): A derivative action on behalf of a limited partnership may not be voluntarily dismissed or settled without the court's approval.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
In this part:Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(1): "Acquired entity" means the entity, all of one or more classes or series of interests in which are acquired in an interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(2): "Acquiring entity" means the entity that acquires all of one or more classes or series of interests of the acquired entity in an interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(3): 48-2e-1141; 48-2e-1146 "Conversion" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(4): "Converted entity" means the converting entity as it continues in existence after a conversion.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(5): 48-2e-1143 "Converting entity" means the domestic entity that approves a plan of conversion pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(6): "Distributional interest" means the right under an unincorporated entity's organic law and organic rules to receive distributions from the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(7): "Domestic," with respect to an entity, means governed as to its internal affairs by the law of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(8): "Domesticated limited partnership" means the domesticating limited partnership as it continues in existence after a domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(9): 48-2e-1153 "Domesticating limited partnership" means the domestic limited partnership that approves a plan of domestication pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(10): 48-2e-1151; 48-2e-1156 "Domestication" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11): 48-1d-202(3) "Entity":
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a): means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(i): a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(ii): a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(iii): a general partnership, including a limited liability partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(iv): a limited partnership, including a limited liability limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(v): a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(vi): a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(vii): an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(viii): a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(ix): any other person that has:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(ix)(A): a legal existence separate from any interest holder of that person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(a)(ix)(B): the power to acquire an interest in real property in its own name; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(b): 48-1d-202(3) does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(b)(i): an individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(b)(ii): a trust with a predominantly donative purpose, or a charitable trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(b)(iii): 48-1d-202(3) an association or relationship that is not a partnership solely by reason of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(b)(iv): a decedent's estate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(11)(b)(v): a government or a governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(12): "Filing entity" means an entity whose formation requires the filing of a public organic record.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(13): "Foreign," with respect to an entity, means an entity governed as to its internal affairs by the law of a jurisdiction other than this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(14): "Governance interest" means a right under the organic law or organic rules of an unincorporated entity, other than as a governor, agent, assignee, or proxy, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(14)(a): receive or demand access to information concerning, or the books and records of, the entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(14)(b): vote for or consent to the election of the governors of the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(14)(c): receive notice of or vote on or consent to an issue involving the internal affairs of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15): "Governor" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(a): a director of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(b): a director or trustee of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(c): a general partner of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(d): a general partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(e): a manager of a manager-managed limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(f): a member of a member-managed limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(g): a director of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(h): a manager of an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(i): a trustee of a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(15)(j): any other person under whose authority the powers of an entity are exercised and under whose direction the activities and affairs of the entity are managed pursuant to the organic law and organic rules of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16): "Interest" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(a): a share in a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(b): a membership in a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(c): a partnership interest in a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(d): a partnership interest in a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(e): a membership interest in a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(f): a member's interest in a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(g): a membership in an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(h): a beneficial interest in a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(16)(i): a governance interest or distributional interest in any other type of unincorporated entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(17): 48-2e-1131; 48-2e-1136 "Interest exchange" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18): "Interest holder" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(a): a shareholder of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(b): a member of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(c): a general partner of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(d): a general partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(e): a limited partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(f): a member of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(g): a member of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(h): a member of an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(i): a beneficiary or beneficial owner of a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(18)(j): any other direct holder of an interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(19): "Interest holder liability" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(19)(a): personal liability for a liability of an entity which is imposed on a person:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(19)(a)(i): solely by reason of the status of the person as an interest holder; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(19)(a)(ii): by the organic rules of the entity which make one or more specified interest holders or categories of interest holders liable in their capacity as interest holders for all or specified liabilities of the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(19)(b): an obligation of an interest holder under the organic rules of an entity to contribute to the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(20): "Jurisdiction of formation" means the jurisdiction whose law includes the organic law of an entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(21): 48-2e-1121; 48-2e-1126 "Merger" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(22): "Merging entity" means an entity that is a party to a merger and exists immediately before the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(23): "Organic law" means the law of an entity's jurisdiction of formation governing the internal affairs of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(24): "Organic rules" means the public organic record and private organic rules of an entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(25): "Plan" means a plan of merger, plan of interest exchange, plan of conversion, or plan of domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(26): 48-2e-1142 "Plan of conversion" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(27): 48-2e-1152 "Plan of domestication" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(28): 48-2e-1132 "Plan of interest exchange" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(29): 48-2e-1122 "Plan of merger" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30): "Private organic rules" means the rules, whether or not in a record, that govern the internal affairs of an entity, are binding on all its interest holders, and are not part of its public organic record, if any.  The term includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30)(a): the bylaws of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30)(b): the bylaws of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30)(c): the partnership agreement of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30)(d): the partnership agreement of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30)(e): the operating agreement of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30)(f): the bylaws of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30)(g): the governing principles of an unincorporated nonprofit association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(30)(h): the trust instrument of a statutory trust or similar rules of a business trust or a common-law business trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(31): "Protected agreement" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(31)(a): a record evidencing indebtedness and any related agreement in effect on January 1, 2014;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(31)(b): an agreement that is binding on an entity on January 1, 2014;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(31)(c): the organic rules of an entity in effect on January 1, 2014; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(31)(d): an agreement that is binding on any of the governors or interest holders of an entity on January 1, 2014.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(32): "Public organic record" means the record, the filing of which by the division is required to form an entity, and any amendment to or restatement of that record.  The term includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(32)(a): the articles of incorporation of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(32)(b): the articles of incorporation of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(32)(c): the certificate of limited partnership of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(32)(d): the certificate of organization of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(32)(e): the articles of organization of a limited cooperative association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(32)(f): the certificate of trust of a statutory trust or similar record of a business trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(33): "Registered foreign entity" means a foreign entity that is registered to do business in this state pursuant to a record filed by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(34): 48-2e-1145 "Statement of conversion" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(35): 48-2e-1155 "Statement of domestication" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(36): 48-2e-1135 "Statement of interest exchange" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(37): 48-2e-1125 "Statement of merger" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(38): "Surviving entity" means the entity that continues in existence after or is created by a merger.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(39): "Type of entity" means a generic form of entity:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(39)(a): recognized at common law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1101(39)(b): formed under an organic law, whether or not some entities formed under that organic law are subject to provisions of that law that create different categories of the form of entity.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1102 Relationship of part to other laws.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
This part does not authorize an act prohibited by, and does not affect the application or requirements of, law other than this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1103 Required notice or approval.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1103(1): A domestic or foreign entity that is required to give notice to, or obtain the approval of, a governmental agency or officer of this state to be a party to a merger must give the notice or obtain the approval to be a party to an interest exchange, conversion, or domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1103(2): Property held for a charitable purpose under the law of this state by a domestic or foreign entity immediately before a transaction under this part becomes effective may not, as a result of the transaction, be diverted from the objects for which it was donated, granted, devised, or otherwise transferred unless, to the extent required by or pursuant to the law of this state concerning cy pres or other law dealing with nondiversion of charitable assets, the entity obtains a court order specifying the disposition of the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1103(3): A bequest, devise, gift, grant, or promise contained in a will or other instrument of donation, subscription, or conveyance that is made to a merging entity that is not the surviving entity and that takes effect or remains payable after the merger inures to the surviving entity.  A trust obligation that would govern property if transferred to the nonsurviving entity applies to property that is transferred to the surviving entity under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1104 Status of filings.
---------------------------------------------------
A filing under this part signed by a domestic entity becomes part of the public organic record of the entity if the entity's organic law provides that similar filings under that law become part of the public organic record of the entity.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1105 Nonexclusivity.
------------------------------------------------
The fact that a transaction under this part produces a certain result does not preclude the same result from being accomplished in any other manner permitted by law other than this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1106 Reference to external facts.
-------------------------------------------------------------
A plan may refer to facts ascertainable outside the plan if the manner in which the facts will operate upon the plan is specified in the plan.  The facts may include the occurrence of an event or a determination or action by a person, whether or not the event, determination, or action is within the control of a party to the transaction.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1107 Alternative means of approval of transactions.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or organic rules of a domestic entity, approval of a transaction under this part by the unanimous vote or consent of its interest holders satisfies the requirements of this part for approval of the transaction.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1108 Appraisal rights.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1108(1): An interest holder of a domestic merging, acquired, converting, or domesticating entity is entitled to appraisal rights in connection with the transaction if the interest holder would have been entitled to appraisal rights under the entity's organic law in connection with a merger in which the interest of the interest holder was changed, converted, or exchanged unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1108(1)(a): the organic law permits the organic rules to limit the availability of appraisal rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1108(1)(b): the organic rules provide such a limit.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1108(2): An interest holder of a domestic merging, acquired, converting, or domesticating entity is entitled to contractual appraisal rights in connection with a transaction under this part to the extent provided in:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1108(2)(a): the entity's organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1108(2)(b): the plan.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1121 Merger authorized.
---------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1121(1)(a): one or more domestic limited partnerships may merge with one or more domestic or foreign entities into a domestic or foreign surviving entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1121(1)(b): two or more foreign entities may merge into a domestic limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1121(2): 48-2e-1121; 48-2e-1126; 48-2e-1121; 48-2e-1126 By complying with the provisions of Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122 Plan of merger.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(1): 48-2e-1121; 48-2e-1126 A domestic limited partnership may become a party to a merger under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(1)(a): as to each merging entity, its name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(1)(b): if the surviving entity is to be created in the merger, a statement to that effect and the entity's name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(1)(c): the manner of converting the interests in each party to the merger into interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(1)(d): if the surviving entity exists before the merger, any proposed amendments to its public organic record, if any, or to its private organic rules that are, or are proposed to be, in a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(1)(e): if the surviving entity is to be created in the merger, its proposed public organic record, if any, and the full text of its private organic rules that are proposed to be in a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(1)(f): the other terms and conditions of the merger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(1)(g): any other provision required by the law of a merging entity's jurisdiction of formation or the organic rules of a merging entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1122(2): (1) In addition to the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1123 Approval of merger.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1123(1): A plan of merger is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1123(1)(a): by a domestic merging limited partnership, by all the partners of the limited partnership entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1123(1)(b): in a record, by each partner of a domestic merging limited partnership that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the merger becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1123(1)(b)(i): the partnership agreement of the limited partnership in a record provides for the approval of a merger in which some or all of its partners become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the partners; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1123(1)(b)(ii): the partner consented in a record to or voted for that provision of the partnership agreement or became a partner after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1123(2): A merger involving a domestic merging entity that is not a limited partnership is not effective unless the merger is approved by that entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1123(3): A merger involving a foreign merging entity is not effective unless the merger is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124 Amendment or abandonment of plan of merger.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(1): A plan of merger may be amended only with the consent of each party to the plan, except as otherwise provided in the plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(2): A domestic merging limited partnership may approve an amendment of a plan of merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(2)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(2)(b): by the partners in the manner provided in the plan, but a partner that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the merger is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(2)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by the interest holders of any party to the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(2)(b)(ii): the public organic record, if any, or private organic rules of the surviving entity that will be in effect immediately after the merger becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the interest holders of the surviving entity under its organic law or organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(2)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the partner in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(3): After a plan of merger has been approved and before a statement of merger becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic merging limited partnership may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(4): If a plan of merger is abandoned after a statement of merger has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by a party to the plan, must be delivered to the division for filing before the statement of merger becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the merger is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(4)(a): the name of each party to the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(4)(b): the date on which the statement of merger was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1124(4)(c): a statement that the merger has been abandoned in accordance with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125 Statement of merger.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(1): A statement of merger must be signed by each merging entity and delivered to the division for filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(2): 48-2e-1121; 48-2e-1126; 48-2e-1126(5) A statement of merger must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(2)(a): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of each merging entity that is not the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(2)(b): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(2)(c): 48-2e-1121; 48-2e-1126 a statement that the merger was approved by each domestic merging entity, if any, in accordance with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(2)(d): if the surviving entity exists before the merger and is a domestic filing entity, any amendment to its public organic record approved as part of the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(2)(e): if the surviving entity is created by the merger and is a domestic filing entity, its public organic record, as an attachment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(2)(f): if the surviving entity is created by the merger and is a domestic limited liability partnership, its statement of qualification, as an attachment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(2)(g): 48-2e-1126(5) if the surviving entity is a foreign entity that is not a registered foreign entity, a mailing address to which the division may send any process served on the division pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(3): (2) In addition to the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(4): If the surviving entity is a domestic entity, its public organic record, if any, must satisfy the requirements of the law of this state, but the public organic record does not need to be signed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1125(5): (2); (5); (5) A plan of merger that is signed by all the merging entities and meets all the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126 Effect of merger.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1): 48-2e-1108 When a merger becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(a): the surviving entity continues or comes into existence;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(b): each merging entity that is not the surviving entity ceases to exist;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(c): all property of each merging entity vests in the surviving entity without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(d): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of each merging entity are debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(e): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of merger, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of each merging entity vest in the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(f): if the surviving entity exists before the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(f)(i): all its property continues to be vested in it without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(f)(ii): it remains subject to all its debts, obligations, and other liabilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(f)(iii): all its rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes continue to be vested in it;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(g): the name of the surviving entity may be substituted for the name of any merging entity that is a party to any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(h): if the surviving entity exists before the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(h)(i): its public organic record, if any, is amended as provided in the statement of merger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(h)(ii): its private organic rules that are to be in a record, if any, are amended to the extent provided in the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(i): if the surviving entity is created by the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(i)(i): its public organic record, if any, is effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(i)(ii): its private organic rules are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(1)(j): 48-2e-1108 the interests in each merging entity which are to be converted in the merger are converted, and the interest holders of those interests are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of merger and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(2): Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or organic rules of a merging entity, the merger does not give rise to any rights that an interest holder, governor, or third party would otherwise have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the merging entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(3): When a merger becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to any of the merging entities and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the merger has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of that entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(4): (4)(a); (4)(a) When a merger becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic merging entity with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(4)(a): The merger does not discharge any interest holder liability under the organic law of the domestic merging entity to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the merger became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(4)(b): The person does not have interest holder liability under the organic law of the domestic merging entity for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(4)(c): (4)(a) The organic law of the domestic merging entity continues to apply to the release, collection, or discharge of any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(4)(d): (4)(a) The person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the organic rules of the domestic merging entity with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(5): 16-17-301 When a merger becomes effective, a foreign entity that is the surviving entity may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any debts, obligations, or other liabilities of a domestic merging entity as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1126(6): When a merger becomes effective, the registration to do business in this state of any foreign merging entity that is not the surviving entity is canceled.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1131(1)(b): all of one or more classes or series of interests of a domestic limited partnership may be acquired by another domestic or foreign entity in exchange for interests, securities, obligations, rights to acquire interests or securities, money, or other property, or any combination of the foregoing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1131(2): 48-2e-1131; 48-2e-1136; 48-2e-1131; 48-2e-1136 By complying with the provisions of Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133 Approval of interest exchange.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133(1): A plan of interest exchange is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133(1)(a): by all the partners of a domestic acquired limited partnership entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133(1)(b): in a record, by each partner of the domestic acquired limited partnership that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the interest exchange becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133(1)(b)(i): the partnership agreement of the limited partnership in a record provides for the approval of an interest exchange or a merger in which some or all of its partners become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all of the partners; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133(1)(b)(ii): the partner consented in a record to or voted for that provision of the partnership agreement or became a partner after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133(2): An interest exchange involving a domestic acquired entity that is not a limited partnership is not effective unless it is approved by the domestic entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133(3): An interest exchange involving a foreign acquired entity is not effective unless it is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1133(4): Except as otherwise provided in its organic law or organic rules, the interest holders of the acquiring entity are not required to approve the interest exchange.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134 Amendment or abandonment of plan of interest exchange.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(1): A plan of interest exchange may be amended only with the consent of each party to the plan, except as otherwise provided in the plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(2): A domestic acquired limited partnership may approve an amendment of a plan of interest exchange:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(2)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(2)(b): by the partners of the limited partnership in the manner provided in the plan, but a partner that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the interest exchange is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(2)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by any of the partners of the acquired limited partnership under the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(2)(b)(ii): the certificate of limited partnership or partnership agreement of the acquired limited partnership that will be in effect immediately after the interest exchange becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the partners of the acquired limited partnership under this chapter or the partnership agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(2)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the partner in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(3): After a plan of interest exchange has been approved and before a statement of interest exchange becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic acquired limited partnership may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(4): If a plan of interest exchange is abandoned after a statement of interest exchange has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by the acquired limited partnership, must be delivered to the division for filing before the statement of interest exchange becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the interest exchange is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(4)(a): the name of the acquired limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(4)(b): the date on which the statement of interest exchange was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1134(4)(c): a statement that the interest exchange has been abandoned in accordance with this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136 Effect of interest exchange.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(1): 48-2e-1108 When an interest exchange in which the acquired entity is a domestic limited partnership becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(1)(a): 48-2e-1108 the interests in the domestic acquired limited partnership that are the subject of the interest exchange cease to exist or are converted or exchanged, and the partners holding those interests are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of interest exchange and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(1)(b): the acquiring entity becomes the interest holder of the interests in the acquired limited partnership stated in the plan of interest exchange to be acquired by the acquiring entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(1)(c): the certificate of limited partnership of the acquired limited partnership is amended as provided in the statement of interest exchange; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(1)(d): the provisions of the partnership agreement of the acquired limited partnership that are to be in a record, if any, are amended to the extent provided in the plan of interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(2): Except as otherwise provided in the partnership agreement of a domestic acquired limited partnership, the interest exchange does not give rise to any rights that a partner or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the acquired limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(3): When an interest exchange becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to a domestic acquired limited partnership and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the interest exchange has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the interest exchange becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(4): (4)(a) When an interest exchange becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic acquired limited partnership with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(4)(a): The interest exchange does not discharge any interest holder liability to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the interest exchange became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(4)(b): The person does not have interest holder liability for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the interest exchange becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1136(4)(c): (4)(a) The person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by other law, this chapter, or the partnership agreement of the acquired entity with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1143 Approval of conversion.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1143(1): A plan of conversion is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1143(1)(a): by a domestic converting limited partnership by all of the partners of the limited partnership entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1143(1)(b): in a record, by each partner of a domestic converting limited partnership that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the conversion becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1143(1)(b)(i): the partnership agreement of the limited partnership provides in a record for the approval of a conversion or a merger in which some or all of its partners become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the interest holders; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1143(1)(b)(ii): the partner voted for or consented in a record to that provision of the partnership agreement or became a partner after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1143(2): A conversion involving a domestic converting entity that is not a limited partnership, including a subject entity, is not effective unless it is approved by the domestic converting entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1143(3): A conversion of a foreign converting entity is not effective unless it is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144 Amendment or abandonment of plan of conversion.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(1): A plan of conversion of a subject entity or domestic converting limited partnership may be amended:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(1)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(1)(b): by the partners of the limited partnership in the manner provided in the plan, but a partner that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the conversion is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(1)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by any of the partners of the converting entity under the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(1)(b)(ii): the public organic record or private organic rules of the converted entity that will be in effect immediately after the conversion becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the interest holders of the converted entity under its organic law or organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(1)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the partner in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(2): After a plan of conversion has been approved and before a statement of conversion becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic converting limited partnership may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(3): If a plan of conversion is abandoned after a statement of conversion has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by the converting entity, must be delivered to the division for filing before the time the statement of conversion becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the conversion is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(3)(a): the name of the converting subject entity or limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(3)(b): the date on which the statement of conversion was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1144(3)(c): a statement that the conversion has been abandoned in accordance with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145 Statement of conversion.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(1): A statement of conversion must be signed by the converting entity and delivered to the division for filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(2): 48-2e-1141; 48-2e-1146; 48-2e-1146(5) A statement of conversion must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(2)(a): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of the converting entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(2)(b): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of the converted entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(2)(c): 48-2e-1141; 48-2e-1146 if the converting entity is a domestic entity, a statement that the plan of conversion was approved in accordance with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(2)(d): if the converted entity is a domestic filing entity, the text of its public organic record, as an attachment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(2)(e): if the converted entity is a domestic limited liability partnership, the text of its statement of qualification, as an attachment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(2)(f): 48-2e-1146(5) if the converted entity is a foreign entity that is not a registered foreign entity, a mailing address to which the division may send any process served on the division pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(3): (2) In addition to the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(4): If the converted entity is a domestic entity, its public organic record, if any, must satisfy the requirements of the law of this state, but the public organic record does not need to be signed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1145(5): (2); (5); (5) A plan of conversion that is signed by a domestic converting entity and meets all the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146 Effect of conversion.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1): 48-2e-1108 When a conversion in which the converted entity is a subject entity or domestic limited partnership becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(a): the converted entity is:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(a)(i): organized under and subject to this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(a)(ii): the same entity without interruption as the converting entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(b): all property of the converting entity continues to be vested in the converted entity without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(c): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the converting entity continue as debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the converted entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(d): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of conversion, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of the converting entity remain in the converted entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(e): the name of the converted entity may be substituted for the name of the converting entity in any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(f): the provisions of the partnership agreement of the converted entity that are to be in a record, if any, approved as part of the plan of conversion are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(1)(g): 48-2e-1108 the interests in the converting entity are converted, and the interest holders of the converting entity are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of conversion and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(2): Except as otherwise provided in the partnership agreement of a domestic converting limited partnership, the conversion does not give rise to any rights that a partner or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the converting entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(3): When a conversion becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to the converting entity and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the conversion has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the conversion becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(4): (4)(a) When a conversion becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic limited partnership with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(4)(a): The conversion does not discharge any interest holder liability to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the conversion became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(4)(b): The person does not have interest holder liability for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the conversion becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(4)(c): (4)(a) The person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the partnership agreement of the converting entity with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(5): 16-17-301 When a conversion becomes effective, a foreign entity that is the converted entity may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any of its debts, obligations, and other liabilities as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(6): If the converting entity is a registered foreign entity, its registration to do business in this state is canceled when the conversion becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1146(7): A conversion does not require the entity to wind up its affairs and does not constitute or cause the dissolution of the entity.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1151 Domestication authorized.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1151(1): 48-2e-1151; 48-2e-1156 By complying with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1151(2): 48-2e-1151; 48-2e-1156 By complying with the provisions of Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1151(3): If a protected agreement contains a provision that applies to a merger of a domestic limited partnership but does not refer to a domestication, the provision applies to a domestication of the limited partnership as if the domestication were a merger until the provision is amended after January 1, 2014.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152 Plan of domestication.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(1): A domestic limited partnership may become a foreign limited partnership in a domestication by approving a plan of domestication.  The plan must be in a record and contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(1)(a): the name of the domesticating limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(1)(b): the name and jurisdiction of formation of the domesticated limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(1)(c): the manner of converting the interests in the domesticating limited partnership into interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(1)(d): the proposed certificate of limited partnership of the domesticated limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(1)(e): the full text of the partnership agreement of the domesticated limited partnership rights to acquire interests or securities, that are proposed to be in a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(1)(f): the other terms and conditions of the domestication; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(1)(g): any other provision required by the law of this state or the partnership agreement of the domesticating limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1152(2): (1) In addition to the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1153 Approval of domestication.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1153(1): A plan of domestication of a domestic domesticating limited partnership is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1153(1)(a): by all the partners entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1153(1)(b): in a record, by each partner that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the domestication becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1153(1)(b)(i): the partnership agreement of the entity in a record provide for the approval of a domestication or merger in which some or all of its partners become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the partners; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1153(1)(b)(ii): the partner voted for or consented in a record to that provision of the partnership agreement or became a partner after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1153(2): A domestication of a foreign domesticating limited partnership is not effective unless it is approved in accordance with the law of the foreign limited partnership's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154 Amendment or abandonment of plan of domestication.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(1): A plan of domestication of a domestic domesticating limited partnership may be amended:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(1)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(1)(b): by the partners of the limited partnership in the manner provided in the plan, but a partner that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the domestication is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(1)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by any of the partners of the domesticating limited partnership under the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(1)(b)(ii): the certificate of limited partnership or partnership agreement of the domesticated limited partnership that will be in effect immediately after the domestication becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the partners of the domesticated limited partnership under its organic law or partnership agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(1)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the partner in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(2): After a plan of domestication has been approved by a domestic domesticating limited partnership and before a statement of domestication becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, by a domestic domesticating limited partnership may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(3): If a plan of domestication is abandoned after a statement of domestication has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by the limited partnership, must be delivered to the division for filing before the time the statement of domestication becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the domestication is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(3)(a): the name of the domesticating limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(3)(b): the date on which the statement of domestication was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1154(3)(c): a statement that the domestication has been abandoned in accordance with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155 Statement of domestication.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155(1): A statement of domestication must be signed by the domesticating limited partnership and delivered to the division for filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155(2): 48-2e-1151; 48-2e-1156; 48-2e-1156(5) A statement of domestication must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155(2)(a): the name and jurisdiction of formation of the domesticating limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155(2)(b): the name and jurisdiction of formation of the domesticated limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155(2)(c): 48-2e-1151; 48-2e-1156 if the domesticating limited partnership is a domestic limited partnership, a statement that the plan of domestication was approved in accordance with Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155(2)(e): 48-2e-1156(5) if the domesticated foreign limited partnership is not a registered foreign limited partnership, a mailing address to which the division may send any process served on the division pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155(3): (2) In addition to the requirements of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1155(5): (2); (5); (5) A plan of domestication that is signed by a domesticating domestic limited partnership and meets all of the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156 Effect of domestication.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1): 48-2e-1108 When a domestication becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(a): the domesticated limited partnership is:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(a)(i): organized under and subject to the organic law of the domesticated limited partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(a)(ii): the same entity without interruption as the domesticating limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(b): all property of the domesticating limited partnership continues to be vested in the domesticated limited partnership without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(c): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the domesticating limited partnership continue as debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the domesticated limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(d): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of domestication, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of the domesticating limited partnership remain in the domesticated limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(e): the name of the domesticated limited partnership may be substituted for the name of the domesticating limited partnership in any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(f): the certificate of limited partnership of the domesticated limited partnership is effective;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(g): the provisions of the partnership agreement of the domesticated limited partnership that are to be in a record, if any, approved as part of the plan of domestication are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(1)(h): 48-2e-1108 the interests in the domesticating limited partnership are converted to the extent and as approved in connection with the domestication, and the partners of the domesticating limited partnership are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of domestication and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(2): Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or partnership agreement of the domesticating limited partnership, the domestication does not give rise to any rights that a partner or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the domesticating limited partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(3): When a domestication becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to the domesticating limited partnership and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic limited partnership as a result of the domestication has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the domestic limited partnership and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(4): (4)(a) When a domestication becomes effective, the following rules apply:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(4)(a): The domestication does not discharge any interest holder liability under this chapter to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the domestication became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(4)(b): A person does not have interest holder liability under this part for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arise after the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(4)(c): (4)(a) A person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the partnership agreement of a domestic domesticating limited partnership with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(5): 16-17-301 When a domestication becomes effective, a foreign limited partnership that is the domesticated limited partnership may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any of its debts, obligations, and other liabilities as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(6): If the domesticating limited partnership is a registered foreign limited partnership, the registration of the foreign limited partnership is canceled when the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1156(7): A domestication does not require the limited partnership to wind up its affairs and does not constitute or cause the dissolution of the limited partnership.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1201 Uniformity of application and construction.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this chapter, consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among states that enact the uniform act upon which this chapter is based.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1202 Severability clause.
-----------------------------------------------------
If any provision of this chapter or its application to any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect other provisions or applications of this chapter which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this chapter are severable.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1203 Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter modifies, limits, and supersedes the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001 et seq., but this chapter does not modify, limit, or supersede Sec. 101(c) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in Sec. 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7003(b).

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1204 Savings clause.
------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not affect an action commenced, proceeding brought, or right accrued before this chapter takes effect.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1205 Application to existing relationships.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-2e-1205(1)(b): (3); (4) except as otherwise provided in Subsections

Utah Code Annotated - Title 48 - Chapter 3a - Utah Revised Uniform Limited Liability Company Act
************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter may be cited as the "Utah Revised Uniform Limited Liability Company Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(1): 48-3a-201 "Certificate of organization" means the certificate required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(2): 48-3a-402 "Contribution," except in the phrase "right of contribution," means property or a benefit described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(3): "Debtor in bankruptcy" means a person that is the subject of:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(3)(a): an order for relief under Title 11 of the United States Code or a comparable order under a successor statute of general application; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(3)(b): a comparable order under federal, state, or foreign law governing insolvency.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(4): "Distribution" means a transfer of money or other property from a limited liability company to a person on account of a transferable interest or in the person's capacity as a member.  The term:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(4)(a): includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(4)(a)(i): a redemption or other purchase by a limited liability company of a transferable interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(4)(a)(ii): a transfer to a member in return for the member's relinquishment of any right to participate as a member in the management or conduct of the company's activities and affairs or to have access to records or other information concerning the company's activities and affairs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(4)(b): does not include amounts constituting reasonable compensation for present or past service or payments made in the ordinary course of business under a bona fide retirement plan or other bona fide benefits program.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(5): "Division" means the Division of Corporations and Commercial Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(6): "Foreign limited liability company" means an unincorporated entity formed under the law of a jurisdiction other than this state, which would be a limited liability company, including a low-profit limited liability company, if formed under the law of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(7): "Governing person" means a person, alone or in concert with others, by or under whose authority the powers of the limited liability company are exercised and under whose direction the activities and affairs of the limited liability company are managed pursuant to this chapter and the limited liability company's operating agreement.  The term includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(7)(a): a manager of a manager-managed limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(7)(b): a member of a member-managed limited liability company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(7)(c): the chief executive officer of a limited liability company in which officers have been appointed, regardless of the actual designated title.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(8): "Jurisdiction," used to refer to a political entity, means the United States, a state, a foreign country, or a political subdivision of a foreign country.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(9): "Jurisdiction of formation" means, with respect to an entity, the jurisdiction:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(9)(a): under whose law the entity is formed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(9)(b): in the case of a limited liability partnership or foreign limited liability partnership, in which the partnership's statement of qualification is filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(10): Part 10, Merger, Interest Exchange, Conversion, and Domestication; 48-3a-1405 "Limited liability company," except in the phrase "foreign limited liability company," means an entity formed under this chapter or which becomes subject to this chapter under
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(11): Part 13, Low-Profit Limited Liability Companies "Low-profit limited liability company" means a limited liability company meeting the requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(12): 48-3a-407(3) "Manager" means a person that under the operating agreement of a manager-managed limited liability company is responsible, alone or in concert with others, for performing the management functions stated in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(13): 48-3a-407(1) "Manager-managed limited liability company" means a limited liability company that qualifies under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(14): 48-3a-401; 48-3a-1405; 48-3a-602 "Member" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(14)(a): 48-3a-401; 48-3a-1405 has become a member of a limited liability company under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(14)(b): 48-3a-602 has not dissociated under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(15): "Member-managed limited liability company" means a limited liability company that is not a manager-managed limited liability company.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(16): 48-3a-112(1) "Operating agreement" means the agreement, whether or not referred to as an operating agreement and whether oral, implied, in a record, or in any combination thereof, of all the members of a limited liability company, including a sole member, concerning the matters described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(17): 48-3a-201 "Organizer" means a person that acts under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(18): "Person" means an individual, business corporation, nonprofit corporation, partnership, limited partnership, limited liability company, limited cooperative association, unincorporated nonprofit association, statutory trust, business trust, common-law business trust, estate, trust, association, joint venture, public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality, or any other legal or commercial entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(19): "Principal office" means the principal executive office of a limited liability company or foreign limited liability company, whether or not the office is located in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(20): Part 11, Professional Services Companies "Professional services company" means a limited liability company organized in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(21): "Property" means all property, whether real, personal, or mixed or tangible or intangible, or any right or interest therein.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(22): "Record," used as a noun, means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(23): "Registered agent" means an agent of a limited liability company or foreign limited liability company which is authorized to receive service of any process, notice, or demand required or permitted by law to be served on the company.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(27): "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.

The term applies to any fraction of the interest by whomever owned.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(31)(a): formed under the law of a tribe; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(31)(b): at least 51% owned or controlled by the tribe under whose law the limited liability company is formed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-102(32): "Tribe" means a tribe, band, nation, pueblo, or other organized group or community of Indians, including an Alaska Native village that is legally recognized as eligible for and is consistent with a special program, service, or entitlement provided by the United States to Indians because of their status as Indians.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-104 Nature, purpose, and duration of limited liability company.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-104(1): A limited liability company is an entity distinct from its member or members.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-104(2): A limited liability company may have any lawful purpose, regardless of whether for profit.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-104(3): A limited liability company has perpetual duration.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-105 Powers.
---------------------------------------
A limited liability company has the capacity to sue and be sued in its own name and the power to do all things necessary or convenient to carry on its activities and affairs.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-106 Governing law.
----------------------------------------------
The law of this state governs:Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-106(1): the internal affairs of a limited liability company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-106(2): the liability of a member as member and a manager as manager for the debts, obligations, or other liabilities of a limited liability company.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-107 Supplemental principles of law.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Unless displaced by particular provisions of this chapter, the principles of law and equity supplement this chapter.
