Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-912 Action by attorney general.
-----------------------------------------------------------
The attorney general may maintain an action to enjoin a foreign limited liability company from doing business in this state in violation of this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
In this part:Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(1): "Acquired entity" means the entity, all of one or more classes or series of interests which are acquired in an interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(2): "Acquiring entity" means the entity that acquires all of one or more classes or series of interests of the acquired entity in an interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(3): 48-3a-1041; 48-3a-1046 "Conversion" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(4): "Converted entity" means the converting entity as it continues in existence after a conversion.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(5): 48-3a-1043 "Converting entity" means the domestic entity that approves a plan of conversion pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(6): "Distributional interest" means the right under an unincorporated entity's organic law and organic rules to receive distributions from the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(7): "Domestic," with respect to an entity, means governed as to its internal affairs by the law of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(8): "Domesticated limited liability company" means the domesticating limited liability company as it continues in existence after a domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(9): 48-3a-1053 "Domesticating limited liability company" means the domestic limited liability company that approves a plan of domestication pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(10): 48-3a-1051; 48-3a-1056 "Domestication" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11): 48-1d-202(3) "Entity":
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a): means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(i): a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(ii): a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(iii): a general partnership, including a limited liability partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(iv): a limited partnership, including a limited liability limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(v): a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(vi): a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(vii): an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(viii): a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(ix): any other person that has:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(ix)(A): a legal existence separate from any interest holder of that person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(a)(ix)(B): the power to acquire an interest in real property in its own name; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(b): 48-1d-202(3) does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(b)(i): an individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(b)(ii): a trust with a predominantly donative purpose or a charitable trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(b)(iii): 48-1d-202(3) an association or relationship that is not a partnership solely by reason of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(b)(iv): a decedent's estate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(11)(b)(v): a government or a governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(12): "Filing entity" means an entity whose formation requires the filing of a public organic record.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(13): "Foreign," with respect to an entity, means an entity governed as to its internal affairs by the law of a jurisdiction other than this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(14): "Governance interest" means a right under the organic law or organic rules of an unincorporated entity, other than as a governor, agent, assignee, or proxy, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(14)(a): receive or demand access to information concerning, or the books and records of, the entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(14)(b): vote for or consent to the election of the governors of the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(14)(c): receive notice of or vote on or consent to an issue involving the internal affairs of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15): "Governor" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(a): a director of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(b): a director or trustee of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(c): a general partner of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(d): a general partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(e): a manager of a manager-managed limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(f): a member of a member-managed limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(g): a director of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(h): a manager of an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(i): a trustee of a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(15)(j): any other person under whose authority the powers of an entity are exercised and under whose direction the activities and affairs of the entity are managed pursuant to the organic law and organic rules of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16): "Interest" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(a): a share in a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(b): a membership in a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(c): a partnership interest in a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(d): a partnership interest in a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(e): a membership interest in a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(f): a member's interest in a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(g): a membership in an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(h): a beneficial interest in a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(16)(i): a governance interest or distributional interest in any other type of unincorporated entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(17): 48-3a-1031; 48-3a-1036 "Interest exchange" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18): "Interest holder" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(a): a shareholder of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(b): a member of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(c): a general partner of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(d): a general partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(e): a limited partner of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(f): a member of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(g): a member of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(h): a member of an unincorporated nonprofit association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(i): a beneficiary or beneficial owner of a statutory trust, business trust, or common-law business trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(18)(j): any other direct holder of an interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(19): "Interest holder liability" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(19)(a): personal liability for a liability of an entity which is imposed on a person:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(19)(a)(i): solely by reason of the status of the person as an interest holder; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(19)(a)(ii): by the organic rules of the entity which make one or more specified interest holders or categories of interest holders liable in their capacity as interest holders for all or specified liabilities of the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(19)(b): an obligation of an interest holder under the organic rules of an entity to contribute to the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(20): 48-3a-1021; 48-3a-1026 "Merger" means a transaction authorized by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(21): "Merging entity" means an entity that is a party to a merger and exists immediately before the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(22): "Organic law" means the law of an entity's jurisdiction of formation governing the internal affairs of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(23): "Organic rules" means the public organic record and private organic rules of an entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(24): "Plan" means a plan of merger, plan of interest exchange, plan of conversion, or plan of domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(25): 48-3a-1042 "Plan of conversion" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(26): 48-3a-1052 "Plan of domestication" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(27): 48-3a-1032 "Plan of interest exchange" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(28): 48-3a-1022 "Plan of merger" means a plan under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29): "Private organic rules" means the rules, whether or not in a record, that govern the internal affairs of an entity, are binding on all its interest holders, and are not part of its public organic record, if any.  The term includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29)(a): the bylaws of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29)(b): the bylaws of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29)(c): the partnership agreement of a general partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29)(d): the partnership agreement of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29)(e): the operating agreement of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29)(f): the bylaws of a limited cooperative association;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29)(g): the governing principles of an unincorporated nonprofit association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(29)(h): the trust instrument of a statutory trust or similar rules of a business trust or common-law business trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(30): "Protected agreement" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(30)(a): a record evidencing indebtedness and any related agreement in effect on January 1, 2014;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(30)(b): an agreement that is binding on an entity on January 1, 2014;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(30)(c): the organic rules of an entity in effect on January 1, 2014; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(30)(d): an agreement that is binding on any of the governors or interest holders of an entity on January 1, 2014.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(31): "Public organic record" means the record the filing of which by the division is required to form an entity and any amendment to or restatement of that record.  The term includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(31)(a): the articles of incorporation of a business corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(31)(b): the articles of incorporation of a nonprofit corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(31)(c): the certificate of limited partnership of a limited partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(31)(d): the certificate of organization of a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(31)(e): the articles of organization of a limited cooperative association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(31)(f): the certificate of trust of a statutory trust or similar record of a business trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(32): "Registered foreign entity" means a foreign entity that is registered to do business in this state pursuant to a record filed by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(33): 48-3a-1045 "Statement of conversion" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(34): 48-3a-1055 "Statement of domestication" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(35): 48-3a-1035 "Statement of interest exchange" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(36): 48-3a-1025 "Statement of merger" means a statement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(37): "Surviving entity" means the entity that continues in existence after or is created by a merger.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(38): "Type of entity" means a generic form of entity:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(38)(a): recognized at common law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1001(38)(b): formed under an organic law, whether or not some entities formed under that organic law are subject to provisions of that law that create different categories of the form of entity.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1002 Relationship of part to other laws.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
This part does not authorize an act prohibited by, and does not affect the application or requirements of, law other than this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1003 Required notice or approval.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1003(1): A domestic or foreign entity that is required to give notice to, or obtain the approval of, a governmental agency or officer of this state to be a party to a merger must give the notice or obtain the approval to be a party to an interest exchange, conversion, or domestication.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1003(2): Property held for a charitable purpose under the law of this state by a domestic or foreign entity immediately before a transaction under this part becomes effective may not, as a result of the transaction, be diverted from the objects for which it was donated, granted, devised, or otherwise transferred unless, to the extent required by or pursuant to the law of this state concerning cy pres or other law dealing with nondiversion of charitable assets, the entity obtains a court order specifying the disposition of the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1003(3): A bequest, devise, gift, grant, or promise contained in a will or other instrument of donation, subscription, or conveyance that is made to a merging entity that is not the surviving entity and that takes effect or remains payable after the merger inures to the surviving entity.  A trust obligation that would govern property if transferred to the nonsurviving entity applies to property that is transferred to the surviving entity under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1004 Status of filings.
---------------------------------------------------
A filing under this part signed by a domestic entity becomes part of the public organic record of the entity if the entity's organic law provides that similar filings under that law become part of the public organic record of the entity.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1005 Nonexclusivity.
------------------------------------------------
The fact that a transaction under this part produces a certain result does not preclude the same result from being accomplished in any other manner permitted by law other than this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1006 References to external facts.
--------------------------------------------------------------
A plan may refer to facts ascertainable outside the plan if the manner in which the facts will operate upon the plan is specified in the plan.  The facts may include the occurrence of an event or a determination or action by a person, whether or not the event, determination, or action is within the control of a party to the transaction.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1007 Alternative means of approval of transactions.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or organic rules of a domestic entity, approval of a transaction under this part by the unanimous vote or consent of its interest holders satisfies the requirements of this part for approval of the transaction.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1008 Appraisal rights.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1008(1): An interest holder of a domestic merging, acquired, converting, or domesticating entity is entitled to appraisal rights in connection with the transaction if the interest holder would have been entitled to appraisal rights under the entity's organic law in connection with a merger in which the interest of the interest holder was changed, converted, or exchanged unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1008(1)(a): the organic law permits the organic rules to limit the availability of appraisal rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1008(1)(b): the organic rules provide such a limit.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1008(2): An interest holder of a domestic merging, acquired, converting, or domesticating entity is entitled to contractual appraisal rights in connection with a transaction under this part to the extent provided in:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1008(2)(a): the entity's organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1008(2)(b): the plan.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1021 Merger authorized.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1021(1): 48-3a-1021; 48-3a-1026 By complying with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1021(1)(a): one or more domestic limited liability companies may merge with one or more domestic or foreign entities into a domestic or foreign surviving entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1021(1)(b): two or more foreign entities may merge into a domestic limited liability company.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1021(2): 48-3a-1021; 48-3a-1026; 48-3a-1021; 48-3a-1026 By complying with the provisions of Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022 Plan of merger.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(1): 48-3a-1021; 48-3a-1026 A domestic limited liability company may become a party to a merger under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(1)(a): as to each merging entity, its name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(1)(b): if the surviving entity is to be created in the merger, a statement to that effect and the entity's name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(1)(c): the manner of converting the interests in each party to the merger into interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(1)(d): if the surviving entity exists before the merger, any proposed amendments to its public organic record, if any, or to its private organic rules that are, or are proposed to be, in a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(1)(e): if the surviving entity is to be created in the merger, its proposed public organic record, if any, and the full text of its private organic rules that are proposed to be in a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(1)(f): the other terms and conditions of the merger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(1)(g): any other provision required by the law of a merging entity's jurisdiction of formation or the organic rules of a merging entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1022(2): (1) In addition to the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1023 Approval of merger.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1023(1): A plan of merger is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1023(1)(a): by a domestic merging limited liability company, by all the members of the limited liability company entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1023(1)(b): in a record, by each member of a domestic merging limited liability company that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the merger becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1023(1)(b)(i): the operating agreement of the limited liability company in a record provides for the approval of a merger in which some or all of its members become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the members; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1023(1)(b)(ii): the member consented in a record to or voted for that provision of the operating agreement or became a member after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1023(2): A merger involving a domestic merging entity that is not a limited liability company is not effective unless the merger is approved by that entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1023(3): A merger involving a foreign merging entity is not effective unless the merger is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024 Amendment or abandonment of plan of merger.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(1): A plan of merger may be amended only with the consent of each party to the plan, except as otherwise provided in the plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(2): A domestic merging limited liability company may approve an amendment of a plan of merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(2)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(2)(b): by the managers or members in the manner provided in the plan, but a member that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the merger is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(2)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by the interest holders of any party to the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(2)(b)(ii): the public organic record, if any, or private organic rules of the surviving entity that will be in effect immediately after the merger becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the interest holders of the surviving entity under its organic law or organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(2)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the member in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(3): After a plan of merger has been approved and before a statement of merger becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic merging limited liability company may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(4): If a plan of merger is abandoned after a statement of merger has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by a party to the plan, must be delivered to the division for filing before the statement of merger becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the merger is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(4)(a): the name of each party to the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(4)(b): the date on which the statement of merger was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1024(4)(c): a statement that the merger has been abandoned in accordance with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025 Statement of merger.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(1): A statement of merger must be signed by each merging entity and delivered to the division for filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(2): 48-3a-1021; 48-3a-1026; 48-3a-1026(5) A statement of merger must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(2)(a): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of each merging entity that is not the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(2)(b): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(2)(c): 48-3a-1021; 48-3a-1026 a statement that the merger was approved by each domestic merging entity, if any, in accordance with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(2)(d): if the surviving entity exists before the merger and is a domestic filing entity, any amendment to its public organic record approved as part of the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(2)(e): if the surviving entity is created by the merger and is a domestic filing entity, its public organic record, as an attachment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(2)(f): if the surviving entity is created by the merger and is a domestic limited liability partnership, its statement of qualification, as an attachment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(2)(g): 48-3a-1026(5) if the surviving entity is a foreign entity that is not a registered foreign entity, a mailing address to which the division may send any process served on the division pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(3): (2) In addition to the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(4): If the surviving entity is a domestic entity, its public organic record, if any, must satisfy the requirements of the law of this state, but the public organic record does not need to be signed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1025(5): (2); (5); (5) A plan of merger that is signed by all the merging entities and meets all the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026 Effect of merger.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1): 48-3a-1008 When a merger becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(a): the surviving entity continues or comes into existence;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(b): each merging entity that is not the surviving entity ceases to exist;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(c): all property of each merging entity vests in the surviving entity without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(d): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of each merging entity are debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(e): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of merger, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of each merging entity vest in the surviving entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(f): if the surviving entity exists before the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(f)(i): all its property continues to be vested in it without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(f)(ii): it remains subject to all its debts, obligations, and other liabilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(f)(iii): all its rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes continue to be vested in it;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(g): the name of the surviving entity may be substituted for the name of any merging entity that is a party to any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(h): if the surviving entity exists before the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(h)(i): its public organic record, if any, is amended as provided in the statement of merger; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(h)(ii): its private organic rules that are to be in a record, if any, are amended to the extent provided in the plan of merger;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(i): if the surviving entity is created by the merger:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(i)(i): its public organic record, if any, is effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(i)(ii): its private organic rules are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(1)(j): 48-3a-1008 the interests in each merging entity which are to be converted in the merger are converted, and the interest holders of those interests are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of merger and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(2): Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or organic rules of a merging entity, the merger does not give rise to any rights that an interest holder, governor, or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the merging entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(3): When a merger becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to any of the merging entities and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the merger has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of that entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(4): (4)(a); (4)(a) When a merger becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic merging entity with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(4)(a): The merger does not discharge any interest holder liability under the organic law of the domestic merging entity to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the merger became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(4)(b): The person does not have interest holder liability under the organic law of the domestic merging entity for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the merger becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(4)(c): (4)(a) The organic law of the domestic merging entity continues to apply to the release, collection, or discharge of any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(4)(d): (4)(a) The person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the organic rules of the domestic merging entity with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(5): 16-17-301 When a merger becomes effective, a foreign entity that is the surviving entity may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any debts, obligations, or other liabilities of a domestic merging entity as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1026(6): When a merger becomes effective, the registration to do business in this state of any foreign merging entity that is not the surviving entity is canceled.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1031 Interest exchange authorized.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1031(1): 48-3a-1031; 48-3a-1036 By complying with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1031(1)(a): a domestic limited liability company may acquire all of one or more classes or series of interests of another domestic or foreign entity in exchange for interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1031(1)(b): all of one or more classes or series of interests of a domestic limited liability company may be acquired by another domestic or foreign entity in exchange for interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1031(2): 48-3a-1031; 48-3a-1036; 48-3a-1031; 48-3a-1036 By complying with the provisions of Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1031(3): If a protected agreement contains a provision that applies to a merger of a domestic limited liability company but does not refer to an interest exchange, the provision applies to an interest exchange in which the domestic limited liability company is the acquired entity as if the interest exchange were a merger until the provision is amended after January 1, 2014.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1032 Plan of interest exchange.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1032(1): 48-3a-1031; 48-3a-1036 A domestic limited liability company may be the acquired entity in an interest exchange under Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1032(1)(e): the other terms and conditions of the interest exchange; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1032(1)(f): any other provision required by the law of this state or the operating agreement of the acquired entity.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033 Approval of interest exchange.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033(1): A plan of interest exchange is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033(1)(a): by all the members of a domestic acquired limited liability company entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033(1)(b): in a record, by each member of the domestic acquired limited liability company that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the interest exchange becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033(1)(b)(i): the operating agreement of the limited liability company in a record provides for the approval of an interest exchange or a merger in which some or all of its members become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the members; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033(1)(b)(ii): the member consented in a record to or voted for that provision of the operating agreement or became a member after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033(2): An interest exchange involving a domestic acquired entity that is not a limited liability company is not effective unless it is approved by the domestic entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033(3): An interest exchange involving a foreign acquired entity is not effective unless it is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1033(4): Except as otherwise provided in its organic law or organic rules, the interest holders of the acquiring entity are not required to approve the interest exchange.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034 Amendment or abandonment of plan of interest exchange.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(1): A plan of interest exchange may be amended only with the consent of each party to the plan, except as otherwise provided in the plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(2): A domestic acquired limited liability company may approve an amendment of a plan of interest exchange:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(2)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(2)(b): by the managers or members of the domestic acquired limited liability company in the manner provided in the plan, but an interest holder that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the interest exchange is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(2)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by any of the members of the acquired limited liability company under the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(2)(b)(ii): the certificate of organization or operating agreement of the acquired limited liability company that will be in effect immediately after the interest exchange becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the members of the acquired limited liability company under this chapter or the operating agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(2)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the member in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(3): After a plan of interest exchange has been approved and before a statement of interest exchange becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic acquired limited liability company may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(4): If a plan of interest exchange is abandoned after a statement of interest exchange has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by the acquired limited liability company, must be delivered to the division for filing before the statement of interest exchange becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the interest exchange is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(4)(a): the name of the acquired limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(4)(b): the date on which the statement of interest exchange was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1034(4)(c): a statement that the interest exchange has been abandoned in accordance with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1035 Statement of interest exchange.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1035(1): A statement of interest exchange must be signed by a domestic acquired limited liability company and delivered to the division for filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1035(2): 48-3a-1031; 48-3a-1036 A statement of interest exchange must contain:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1035(2)(d): any amendments to the acquired limited liability company's certificate of organization approved as part of the plan of interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1035(3): (2) In addition to the requirements of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036 Effect of interest exchange.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(1): 48-3a-1008 When an interest exchange in which the acquired entity is a domestic limited liability company becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(1)(a): 48-3a-1008 the interests in a domestic limited liability company that are the subject of the interest exchange cease to exist or are converted or exchanged, and the members holding those interests are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of interest exchange and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(1)(b): the acquiring entity becomes the interest holder of the interests in the acquired limited liability company stated in the plan of interest exchange to be acquired by the acquiring entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(1)(c): the certificate of organization of the acquired limited liability company is amended as provided in the statement of interest exchange; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(1)(d): the provisions of the operating agreement of the acquired limited liability company that are to be in a record, if any, are amended to the extent provided in the plan of interest exchange.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(2): Except as otherwise provided in the operating agreement of a domestic acquired limited liability company, the interest exchange does not give rise to any rights that a member, manager, or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the acquired limited liability company.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(3): When an interest exchange becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to a domestic acquired limited liability company and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the interest exchange has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the interest exchange becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(4): (4)(a) When an interest exchange becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic acquired limited liability company with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(4)(a): The interest exchange does not discharge any interest holder liability to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the interest exchange became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(4)(b): The person does not have interest holder liability for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the interest exchange becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1036(4)(c): (4)(a) The person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the operating agreement of the acquired limited liability company with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1041(3)(b): a foreign entity that is a different type of entity, if the conversion is authorized by the law of the foreign jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1041(4): 48-3a-1041; 48-3a-1046 By complying with the provisions of Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1042 Plan of conversion.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1042(1): 48-3a-1041; 48-3a-1046 A subject entity may convert to a domestic limited liability company or a domestic limited liability company may convert to a different type of entity under Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1042(1)(b): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of the converted entity;

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1043 Approval of conversion.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1043(1): A plan of conversion is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1043(1)(a): by a domestic converting limited liability company by all the members of the limited liability company entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1043(1)(b): in a record, by each member of a domestic converting limited liability company that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the conversion becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1043(1)(b)(i): the operating agreement of the limited liability company provides in a record for the approval of a conversion or a merger in which some or all of its interest holders become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the interest holders; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1043(1)(b)(ii): the member voted for or consented in a record to that provision of the operating agreement or became a member after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1043(2): A conversion involving a domestic converting entity that is not a limited liability company, including a subject entity, is not effective unless it is approved by the domestic converting entity in accordance with its organic law.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1043(3): A conversion of a foreign converting entity is not effective unless it is approved by the foreign entity in accordance with the law of the foreign entity's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044 Amendment or abandonment of plan of conversion.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(1): A plan of conversion of a subject entity or domestic converting limited liability company may be amended:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(1)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(1)(b): by the managers or members of the entity in the manner provided in the plan, but a member that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the conversion is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(1)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by any of the interest holders of the converting entity under the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(1)(b)(ii): the public organic record or private organic rules of the converted entity that will be in effect immediately after the conversion becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the interest holders of the converted entity under its organic law or organic rules; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(1)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the interest holder in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(2): After a plan of conversion has been approved and before a statement of conversion becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a subject entity or domestic converting limited liability company may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(3): If a plan of conversion is abandoned after a statement of conversion has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement of conversion becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by the converting entity, must be delivered to the division for filing before the time the statement of conversion becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the conversion is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(3)(a): the name of the converting subject entity or limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(3)(b): the date on which the statement of conversion was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1044(3)(c): a statement that the conversion has been abandoned in accordance with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045 Statement of conversion.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(1): A statement of conversion must be signed by the converting entity and delivered to the division for filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(2): 48-3a-1041; 48-3a-1046; 48-3a-1046(5) A statement of conversion must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(2)(a): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of the converting entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(2)(b): the name, jurisdiction of formation, and type of entity of the converted entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(2)(c): 48-3a-1041; 48-3a-1046 if the converting entity is a domestic entity, a statement that the plan of conversion was approved in accordance with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(2)(d): if the converted entity is a domestic filing entity, the text of its public organic record, as an attachment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(2)(e): if the converted entity is a domestic limited liability partnership, the text of its statement of qualification, as an attachment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(2)(f): 48-3a-1046(5) if the converted entity is a foreign entity that is not a registered foreign entity, a mailing address to which the division may send any process served on the division pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(3): (2) In addition to the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(4): If a converted entity is a domestic entity, its public organic record, if any, must satisfy the requirements of the law of this state, but the public organic record does not need to be signed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1045(5): (2); (5); (5) A plan of conversion that is signed by a domestic converting entity and meets all the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046 Effect of conversion.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1): 48-3a-1008 When a conversion in which the converted entity is a subject entity or domestic limited liability company becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(a): the converted entity is:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(a)(i): organized under and subject to this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(a)(ii): the same entity without interruption as the converting entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(b): all property of the converting entity continues to be vested in the converted entity without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(c): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the converting entity continue as debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the converted entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(d): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of conversion, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of the converting entity remain in the converted entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(e): the name of the converted entity may be substituted for the name of the converting entity in any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(f): the provisions of the operating agreement of the converted entity that are to be in a record, if any, approved as part of the plan of conversion are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(1)(g): 48-3a-1008 the interests in the converting entity are converted, and the interest holders of the converting entity are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of conversion and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(2): Except as otherwise provided in the operating agreement of a domestic converting limited liability company, the conversion does not give rise to any rights that a member, manager, or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the converting entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(3): When a conversion becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to the converting entity and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic entity as a result of the conversion has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the entity and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the conversion becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(4): (4)(a) When a conversion becomes effective, the interest holder liability of a person that ceases to hold an interest in a domestic limited liability company with respect to which the person had interest holder liability is as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(4)(a): the conversion does not discharge any interest holder liability to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the conversion became effective;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(4)(b): the person does not have interest holder liability for any debt, obligation, or other liability that arises after the conversion becomes effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(4)(c): (4)(a) the person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the operating agreement of the converting entity with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(5): 16-17-301 When a conversion becomes effective, a foreign entity that is the converted entity may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any of its debts, obligations, and liabilities as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(6): If the converting entity is a registered foreign entity, the registration to do business in this state of the converting entity is canceled when the conversion becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1046(7): A conversion does not require the entity to wind up its affairs and does not constitute or cause the dissolution of the entity.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1053 Approval of domestication.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1053(1): A plan of domestication of a domestic domesticating limited liability company is not effective unless it has been approved:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1053(1)(a): by all the members entitled to vote on or consent to any matter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1053(1)(b): in a record, by each member that will have interest holder liability for debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the domestication becomes effective, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1053(1)(b)(i): the operating agreement of the entity in a record provides for the approval of a domestication or merger in which some or all of its members become subject to interest holder liability by the vote or consent of fewer than all the members; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1053(1)(b)(ii): the member voted for or consented in a record to that provision of the operating agreement or became an interest holder after the adoption of that provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1053(2): A domestication of a foreign domesticating limited liability company is not effective unless it is approved in accordance with the law of the foreign limited liability company's jurisdiction of formation.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054 Amendment or abandonment of plan of domestication.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(1): A plan of domestication of a domestic domesticating limited liability company may be amended:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(1)(a): in the same manner as the plan was approved, if the plan does not provide for the manner in which it may be amended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(1)(b): by the managers or members of the limited liability company in the manner provided in the plan, but a member that was entitled to vote on or consent to approval of the domestication is entitled to vote on or consent to any amendment of the plan that will change:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(1)(b)(i): the amount or kind of interests, securities, obligations, money, other property, rights to acquire interests or securities, or any combination of the foregoing, to be received by any of the interest holders of the domesticating limited liability company under the plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(1)(b)(ii): the certificate of organization or operating agreement of the domesticated limited liability company that will be in effect immediately after the domestication becomes effective, except for changes that do not require approval of the members of the domesticated limited liability company under its organic law or operating agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(1)(b)(iii): any other terms or conditions of the plan, if the change would adversely affect the interest holder in any material respect.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(2): After a plan of domestication has been approved by a domestic domesticating limited liability company and before a statement of domestication becomes effective, the plan may be abandoned as provided in the plan.  Unless prohibited by the plan, a domestic domesticating limited liability company may abandon the plan in the same manner as the plan was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(3): If a plan of domestication is abandoned after a statement of domestication has been delivered to the division for filing and before the statement of domestication becomes effective, a statement of abandonment, signed by the domesticating limited liability company, must be delivered to the division for filing before the time the statement of domestication becomes effective.  The statement of abandonment takes effect on filing, and the domestication is abandoned and does not become effective.  The statement of abandonment must contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(3)(a): the name of the domesticating limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(3)(b): the date on which the statement of domestication was delivered to the division for filing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1054(3)(c): a statement that the domestication has been abandoned in accordance with this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056 Effect of domestication.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1): 48-3a-1008 When a domestication becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(a): the domesticated limited liability company is:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(a)(i): organized under and subject to the organic law of the domesticated limited liability company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(a)(ii): the same entity without interruption as the domesticating limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(b): all property of the domesticating limited liability company continues to be vested in the domesticated limited liability company without transfer, reversion, or impairment;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(c): all debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the domesticating limited liability company continue as debts, obligations, and other liabilities of the domesticated limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(d): except as otherwise provided by law or the plan of domestication, all the rights, privileges, immunities, powers, and purposes of the domesticating limited liability company remain in the domesticated limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(e): the name of the domesticated limited liability company may be substituted for the name of the domesticating limited liability company in any pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(f): the certificate of organization of the domesticated limited liability company is effective;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(g): the provisions of the operating agreement of the domesticated limited liability company that are to be in a record, if any, approved as part of the plan of domestication are effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(1)(h): 48-3a-1008 the interests in the domesticating limited liability company are converted to the extent and as approved in connection with the domestication, and the members of the domesticating limited liability company are entitled only to the rights provided to them under the plan of domestication and to any appraisal rights they have under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(2): Except as otherwise provided in the organic law or operating agreement of the domesticating limited liability company, the domestication does not give rise to any rights that a member, manager, or third party would have upon a dissolution, liquidation, or winding up of the domesticating limited liability company.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(3): When a domestication becomes effective, a person that did not have interest holder liability with respect to the domesticating limited liability company and becomes subject to interest holder liability with respect to a domestic limited liability company as a result of the domestication has interest holder liability only to the extent provided by the organic law of the domestic limited liability company and only for those debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(4): (4)(a) When a domestication becomes effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(4)(a): The domestication does not discharge any interest holder liability under this chapter to the extent the interest holder liability arose before the domestication became effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(4)(b): A person does not have interest holder liability under this part for any debts, obligations, and other liabilities that arise after the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(4)(c): (4)(a) A person has whatever rights of contribution from any other person as are provided by law other than this chapter, this chapter, or the operating agreement of a domestic domesticating limited liability company with respect to any interest holder liability preserved under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(5): 16-17-301 When a domestication becomes effective, a foreign limited liability company that is the domesticated limited liability company may be served with process in this state for the collection and enforcement of any of its debts, obligations, and liabilities as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(6): If the domesticating limited liability company is a registered foreign limited liability company, the registration of the foreign limited liability company is canceled when the domestication becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1056(7): A domestication does not require the limited liability company to wind up its affairs and does not constitute or cause the dissolution of the company.

---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1101(1): Title 58, Chapter 26a, Certified Public Accountant Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 3a, Architects Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 73, Chiropractic Physician Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 69, Dentist and Dental Hygienist Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 22, Professional Engineers and Professional Land Surveyors Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 71, Naturopathic Physician Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 31b, Nurse Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 44a, Nurse Midwife Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 16a, Utah Optometry Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 68, Utah Osteopathic Medical Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 17b, Pharmacy Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 67, Utah Medical Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 70a, Utah Physician Assistant Act; Title 58, Chapter 24b, Physical Therapy Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 5a, Podiatric Physician Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 61, Psychologist Licensing Act; Title 61, Chapter 2f, Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act; Title 58, Chapter 60, Part 2, Social Worker Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 60, Mental Health Professional Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 28, Veterinary Practice Act; Title 61, Chapter 2g, Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Act "Professional services" means a personal service provided by:

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1102 Application of this part.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1102(1): If a conflict arises between this part and another provision of this chapter, this part controls.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1102(2): Notwithstanding the other provisions of this part, on and after January 1, 2016:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1102(2)(a): a professional services company may not designate series of transferable interests; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1102(2)(b): a limited liability company may not form a professional services company as a series of the limited liability company.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1105 Providing a professional service.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1105(1): 48-3a-1106 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1105(2): (1) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1105(2)(a): require an individual employed by a professional services company to be licensed to perform a service for the professional services company if a license is not otherwise required;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1105(2)(b): prohibit a licensed individual from providing a professional service in the individual's professional capacity although the individual is a member, manager, employee, or agent of a professional services company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1105(2)(c): prohibit an individual licensed in another state from providing a professional service for a professional services company in this state if not prohibited by the regulating board.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106 Limit of one profession.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(1): (1)(a) A professional services company organized to provide a professional service under this part may provide only:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(1)(a): one specific type of professional service; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(1)(b): (1)(a) services ancillary to the professional service described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(2): (2)(a) A professional services company organized to provide a professional service under this part may not engage in a business other than to provide:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(2)(a): the professional service that it was organized to provide; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(2)(b): (2)(a) services ancillary to the professional service described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(3): (1); (2) Notwithstanding Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(3)(a): own real and personal property necessary or appropriate for providing the type of professional service it was organized to provide; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(3)(b): invest the professional services company's money in one or more of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(3)(b)(i): real estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(3)(b)(ii): mortgages;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(3)(b)(iii): stocks;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(3)(b)(iv): bonds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1106(3)(b)(v): another type of investment.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1107 Activity limitations.
------------------------------------------------------
A professional services company may not do anything that an individual licensed to practice the profession that the professional services company is organized to provide is prohibited from doing.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1108 This part does not limit regulating board.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
This part does not restrict the authority or duty of a regulating board to license an individual providing a professional service or the practice of the profession that is within the jurisdiction of the regulating board, notwithstanding that the individual:Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1108(1): is a member, manager, or employee of a professional services company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1108(2): provides the professional service or engages in the practice of the profession through a professional services company.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1109 Member or manager of a professional services company.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A professional services company organized to provide a professional service:Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1109(1): may include a member, manager, or employee who is authorized under the laws of the jurisdiction where the member, manager, or employee resides to provide a similar professional service;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1109(2): may include a member who is not licensed or registered by the state to provide the professional service to the extent allowed by the applicable licensing or registration act relating to the professional service; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1109(3): may render a professional service in this state only through a member, manager, or employee who is licensed or registered by this state to render the professional service.

Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112 Conversion to nonprofessional company.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112(1): A professional services company subject to this part converts into a limited liability company subject to this chapter, but not subject to this part on the day on which:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112(1)(a): no member of the professional services company is licensed or registered for the professional service for which the professional services company is organized; or
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112(1)(b): all members entitled to vote on or consent to any matter consent not to be a professional services company subject to this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112(2): (1); (1) A professional services company converted as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112(3): A limited liability company resulting from a conversion under this section may reconvert to a professional services company:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112(3)(a): upon at least one member of the limited liability company being licensed or registered for the professional service for which the limited liability company is organized; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112(3)(b): each member of the limited liability company entitled to vote on or consent to any matter consents to reconvert the limited liability company to a professional services company subject to this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1112(4): If a professional services company is converted or reconverted under this section, the professional services company shall file a certificate of amendment to the certificate of organization with the division within a reasonable time after the conversion or reconversion to reflect the changes.


Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201 Series of transferable interests.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(1): An operating agreement may establish or provide for the establishment of a designated series of transferable interests having separate rights, powers, or duties with respect to specified property or obligations of the limited liability company or profits and losses associated with specified property or obligations, and, to the extent provided in the operating agreement, any such series may have a separate business purpose or investment objective.  The name of each series must contain the name of the limited liability company and be distinguishable from the name of any other series.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(2): 48-3a-1202 Notwithstanding contrary provisions of this chapter, the debts, liabilities, and obligations incurred, contracted for, or otherwise existing with respect to a particular series shall be enforceable against the assets of that series only, and not against the assets of the limited liability company generally or any other series, if all of the following apply:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(2)(a): the series is established by or in accordance with the operating agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(2)(b): separate and distinct records are maintained for the series;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(2)(c): the assets associated with the series are held and accounted for separately from the other assets of the limited liability company, including another series;
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(2)(d): the operating agreement or the agreement establishing the series provides for the limitation on liabilities of the series; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(2)(e): 48-3a-1202 notice of the limitation on liability of the series is set forth in the limited liability company's certificate of organization in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(3): (2) A series meeting all of the conditions of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(3)(a): be treated as a separate entity to the extent set forth in the certificate of organization; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(3)(b): have the power and capacity to, in its own name, contract, hold title to property, grant liens and security interests, and sue and be sued.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(4): Notwithstanding the other provisions of this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(4)(a): property and assets of a series may not be transferred to the limited liability company generally or another series if the transfer impairs the ability of the series releasing the property or assets to pay its debts existing at the time of the transfer unless fair value is given to the transferring series for the property or assets transferred; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(4)(b): a tax or other liability of the limited liability company generally or of a series may not be assigned by the series against which the tax or other liability is imposed to the limited liability company generally or to another series within the limited liability company if the assignment impairs a creditor's right and ability to fully collect an amount due when owed.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(5): Notwithstanding the other provisions of this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(5)(a): a professional services company may not designate a series of transferable interests; and
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(5)(b): a limited liability company may not form a professional services company as a series of the limited liability company.
Utah Code Annotated § 48-3a-1201(6): Except to the extent modified by this part, the provisions of this chapter which are generally applicable to a limited liability company, and its managers, members, and transferees, shall be applicable to each series with respect to the operations of such a series.
